Megan Rose Dickey
Senior Reporter


Megan Rose Dickey is a senior reporter at TechCrunch focused on labor, transportation, and diversity and inclusion in tech.
She previously spent two years at Business Insider covering tech startups focused on the shared economy, IoT and music industry.
She graduated from the University of Southern California in 2011 with a degree in Broadcast and Digital Journalism.

Since Russian troops invaded Ukraine in late February, Delfast\u2019s top priority has been to see its Ukrainian team of 30 safely evacuated from the most dangerous parts of the country.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n When not focusing on sales, marketing, R&D and customer support, Delfast\u2019s smaller team of seven employees based in Los Angeles has been pleading with U.S. politicians and the European Commission to supply Ukraine with anti-aircraft missiles and fighter jets that could help Ukraine gain back some control over its air space, and, hopefully, put a stop to this war.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Delfast\u2019s co-founders, Daniel Tonkopi and Serhiy Denysenko, say they have always believed in safeguarding the future. When they founded Delfast in 2014, originally as a delivery company, Tonkoply and Denysenko knew that providing couriers with green transportation options would be critical to the company\u2019s operations.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n \t \n\t\t \n\t\t\tThe most important thing for an entrepreneur, and in general for any leader, is to protect the team and be completely honest with them during a tough time.\t\t\t\t\t\t\tDaniel Tonkopi, co-founder of Delfast<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/span><\/p>\n The founders soon realized that a bike with the power, range and battery life their couriers needed didn\u2019t exist, and so they set out to build one. In 2017, backed by a Kickstarter campaign that saw the company raise $165,000, the startup began manufacturing a bike to fit its needs \u2013 one that promptly <\/span>won the Guinness Book of World Records<\/span><\/a> for the greatest distance traveled on an electric motorbike on a single charge.<\/span><\/p>\n More recently, the Delfast Top 3.0 e-motorbike <\/span>won Forbes\u2019 fastest e-bike of the year<\/span><\/a> in 2022 after the company announced some serious <\/span>upgrades to the vehicle during CES<\/span><\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n We spoke with Delfast\u2019s co-founders to discuss what it\u2019s like running a startup during a war, how the startup is considering breaking into new business verticals, and the importance of always having a Plan B.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n The following interview, part of an ongoing series with founders who are building transportation companies, has been edited for length and clarity.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n Note: Serhiy Denysenko\u2019s answers were translated from Ukrainian by a member of Delfast\u2019s team for TechCrunch.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n TC: Serhiy, you’re on the ground in Kyiv. What’s your day-to-day like?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. It\u2019s important to keep in touch and know that everyone is fine, or as fine as is possible right now.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Besides my work as a COO, I\u2019ve been helping with volunteering, getting supplies and medicine to people, and this is something that pretty much every Ukrainian is now doing. I had my family relocated to Hungary, so I feel more or less safe, and I\u2019m just trying to work as much as possible and do my best in every possible area, whether that\u2019s supporting the company or supporting Ukraine in general.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n How are you managing your team through this crisis? What\u2019s changed?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>We got used to working remotely during Coronavirus times, so we have our task tracker, where everyone can see his or her task. Every Monday, we have an online Zoom meeting. Previously we only had these meetings at the executive level, but now during the war, we are gathering all together, just to see each other\u2019s faces and ask how they\u2019re doing, how\u2019s everyone feeling. Just to talk with everybody.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n <\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" “Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. the robo-berry"},"content":{"rendered":" If you’ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that’s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren’t super good at because they tend to be… crushy. But this robo-berry<\/a> designed by Swiss researchers could usher in a new era of gentle, automated robo-pickers.<\/p>\n The secret to picking a raspberry is to grip it just enough to get purchase and then pull it downwards off the little stem, apparently called the “receptacle,” which seems backwards. Seems simple \u2014 and it is, but only our hands are among the most sensitive and finely controlled constructions in the universe, the culmination of a hundred million years of evolution, outdone only by (I suspect) raccoons.<\/p>\n Robots simply don’t have the senses necessary to figure out the perfect technique for picking a berry. But what if it could communicate with the berry to better sense the forces involved and avoid either a a brutal crushing or humiliating failure-to-detach?<\/p> <\/div>\n That’s what Kai Junge, a PhD student at EPFL in Switzerland, aims to accomplish with this “sensorized raspberry,” a silicone and silicon replica berry that provides feedback to the picking machine, allowing it to learn to pick faster and better \u2014 and cleaner.<\/p>\n “It\u2019s an exciting dilemma for us as robotics engineers,” said professor Josie Hughes, who worked with Junge on the project. “The raspberry harvesting season is so short, and the fruit is so valuable, that wasting them simply isn’t an option. What’s more, the cost and logistical challenges of testing different options out in the field are prohibitive. That\u2019s why we decided to run our tests in the lab and develop a replica raspberry for training harvesting robots.”<\/p>\n Apparently the hard part comes just at the moment of detaching, when the force needed to grip the berry on the receptacle suddenly becomes overkill as the object goes from solid to hollow.<\/p>\n The replica berry has a fluidic sensor that tells the system how much compression is being experienced by the silicone drooplets, allowing the control model to learn how to adjust its grip as if the berry itself is telling it how much is too much.<\/p>\n You can see the berry in action below:<\/p>\n <\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The team plans to present their work at RobotSoft in April. And once the raspberry question is decided, they may move on to other berries, tomatoes, grapes&#8230; even apricots. The future is looking fresh!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you&#8217;ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that&#8217;s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren&#8217;t super good at because they tend to be&#8230; crushy. -companies?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=8191"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292389,"date":"2022-03-31T11:55:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T18:55:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292389"},"modified":"2022-03-31T17:57:31","modified_gmt":"2022-04-01T00:57:31","slug":"all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination\/","title":{"rendered":"All eyes are on Swvl as it starts trading on a SPAC combination"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mass transit and shared mobility provider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swvl.com\/\">Swvl<\/a> went public today in <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its shares at $10 on the Nasdaq through a merger with U.S. women-led blank check company Queen\u2019s Gambit Growth Capital. The planned merger, which will see Swvl offer 20-30% of its total shares, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">announced last July<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Following closing, the combined company, now \u201cSwvl Holding Corp,\u201d will trade under GMBT and GMBTW today before switching to SWVL and SWVLW on April 1.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292389\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl is the first company launched from Africa and the second Middle Eastern company to list on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Anghami, an Abu Dhabi-based music streaming platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">did so in February<\/a> when it listed with Vistas Media Acquisition at a $220 million valuation.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/embed\/#?secret=CnJTROn2h9#?secret=Q5eMhyfACo\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl raised $121.5 million in private investment in public equities (PIPE) for this transaction<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), Teklas Ventures, Chimera, Agility, and Luxor Capital Group are some of its other investors. The company is currently valued at $1.5 billion.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February, one of its investors, Atalaya Capital, pulled out of the transaction. And in a filing, Queen\u2019s Gambit announced the termination of forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreements worth $100 million in SPAC shares and an extra $2 million via a private placement.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreement <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was done<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> with a group, and it was <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> access to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> capital,\u201d Queen\u2019s Gambit Capital founder and CEO Victoria Grace told TechCrunch when asked if the termination affects the deal.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIts termination doesn\u2019t affect the valuation of the company or anything around our fundamental deal, which is Queen\u2019s Gambit merging with SWVL, so the valuation [stays] the same,\u201d she said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors withdrawing their interests and dollars from SPACs is not peculiar to Swvl. It\u2019s a usual occurrence &#8212; for instance, when BuzzFeed went public last December, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\">94% of the $287.5 million raised by the SPAC <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was withdrawn<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> &#8212; particularly as the SPAC hype gives way in the face of an underperforming market and tighter regulation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite the seeming setback, there\u2019s good news for Swvl. <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to CFO Youssef Salem, the company has an <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional $600 million from proceeds and<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> committed equity facility with B. Riley Principal to access over the next few weeks if certain conditions are met, he said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Swvl was founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">Mostafa Kandil<\/a>, Mahmoud Nouh and Ahmed Sabbah in 2017. The trio started the company as a bus-hailing service in Egypt and other ride-sharing services in emerging markets with fragmented public transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Its bus-hailing services enable users to make intra-state journeys by booking seats on buses running a fixed route. Swvl offerings have expanded beyond bus-hailing services, though. Now, the company offers inter-city rides, car ride-sharing, and corporate services in the 10 cities it operates in across Africa and the Middle East.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The partnership between Swvl and Queen\u2019s Gambit came from a mutual interest from both parties<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While searching for a company to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">acquire<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl fit the blank-check company\u2019s criteria: strong business fundamentals, mobility and logistics (one of its core verticals), and an ESG ethos around women and affordable transportation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the other hand<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl &#8212; off the back of raising over $170 million in venture capital, expanding to over 16 countries across Latin America, Asia and Africa; hiring executives from Facebook, Uber and Optimus; and acquiring Shotl, Viapool and door2door &#8212; was on a quest for global dominance in the mobility space. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A SPAC with Queen\u2019s Gambit was the most suitable option for it from a financial standpoint, and both parties feel strongly about the sustainability angle around transport &#8212; Swvl claims it has prevented approximately 289 million pounds of carbon emissions since its inception.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to expand into several countries over the next six months, including Colombia, Mexico, South Africa, and the U.S. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the meantime, all eyes will be on the company\u2019s performance as it <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">officially<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> starts trading tomorrow in a cooling SPAC market and a generally unsettled public market.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThere\u2019s a softness in the market, but as long as the company operates and delivers results, <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">maybe<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> today, people don\u2019t pay attention to it, but they will in months ahead,\u201d Grace said about the worrying SPAC and public markets.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I think<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the market will change <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> like it always does and people go back to fundamentals at how we look at company\u2019s performances. For Swvl, they have been beating every single number that was ever presented to us. And that\u2019s what makes me super excited about this. And that\u2019s the type of target you want to partner with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/\">Almost everything you need to know about SPACs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Almost everything you need to know about SPACs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/embed\/#?secret=dbGVg33T0n#?secret=s9kBhwdIHM\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Mass transit and shared mobility provider Swvl went public today in a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems. /tc_video?tags=21691"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576814951,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/corporate-services\/","name":"corporate services","slug":"corporate-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576814951"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576814951"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":52630,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/dubai\/","name":"Dubai","slug":"dubai","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/52630"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=52630"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292372,"date":"2022-03-31T12:05:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T19:05:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292372"},"modified":"2022-03-31T13:58:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T20:58:42","slug":"microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings\/","title":{"rendered":"Microsoft acquires process mining vendor Minit to grow its automation offerings"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Minit<\/a>, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which of those processes are ripe for automation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Minit currently enables businesses to transform the way they analyze, monitor and optimize their processes. Minit\u2019s solutions have helped businesses gain deep insights into how processes run, uncover root causes of operational challenges and help mitigate undesired process outcomes,&#8221; Justin Graham, Microsoft&#8217;s general manager of process insights, wrote in a <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/blog\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-minit-to-strengthen-process-mining-capabilities\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Microsoft&#8217;s corporate blog. &#8220;[With Minit, our] customers will be able to better understand their process data, uncover what operations look like in reality, and drive process standardization and improvement across the entire organization to ensure compliance at every step.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft dipped its toes into process mining with the launch of new features in Power Automate in 2019 and the acquisition of Softomotive, an RPA software provider, a year later. But with Minit, the tech giant is doubling down on a software category that could be worth over $11 billion by 2030, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wfmz.com\/news\/pr_newswire\/pr_newswire_technology\/global-process-mining-software-market-size-value-estimated-to-reach-usd-11-096-7-million\/article_a95b3354-ec2f-5389-b761-e4dbbdadbb97.html#:~:text=According%20to%20research%20report%20published,forecast%20period%202022%20to%202030.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to a report from Polaris Market Research.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292372\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It wasn&#8217;t immediately clear whether the whole of the Minit team will join Microsoft &#8212; or, indeed, whether the company will remain spread across its current locations. (Minit is now headquartered in Amsterdam, with satellite offices in London and New York.) But CEO James Dening said that customers shouldn&#8217;t expect a change in the level of support they&#8217;re currently receiving.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are looking forward to what it means to become part of an industry leader like Microsoft and what that brings us &#8212; how we can use that scale and excellence to continue to deliver great solutions to our customers,&#8221; Dening wrote in a blog <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/blog\/microsoft-minit-acquisition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Minit&#8217;s website. &#8220;It has been a privilege to lead the company for the last year, and I\u2019m excited to continue my journey with the team, as part of what I consider to be the world\u2019s leading software company.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Microsoft spokesperson Zara Huang told TechCrunch that the Minit team will move into the\u00a0<span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> Process Insights team and that there will be &#8220;no change&#8221; to the current work location of Minit team members. <span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> is in early stages of determining how Minit will be integrated into its offerings, she said, and the companies will share more details when they&#8217;re available.<\/p>\n<p>Minit, which was founded in 2015 by Rasto Hlavac and had raised \u20ac10.3 million (~$11.40 million) prior to the acquisition, is one of an expanding number of startups developing process mining tools aimed at enterprise clientele. Process mining, also known as task discovery, involves spotting root cause workflow issues and bottlenecks by pulling data from systems including desktop, email apps and workflows. It&#8217;s a key part of robotic process automation (RPA), a technology that promises to automate monotonous, repetitive tasks traditionally performed by human workers while at the same time generating logs to identify potential cost savings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As Protocol&#8217;s Aisha Counts <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/microsoft-process-mining-minit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notes<\/a>, process mining has traditionally been done by system integrators who map out processes by analyzing manual workflows. Process mining software is designed to digitize the approach in a way that reduces the expense, time and effort involved.<\/p>\n<p>Underlining the appetite for process mining technologies, Celonis, a data processing company, earlier this week acquired Minit competitor Process Analytics Factory, which coincidentally integrates with Microsoft&#8217;s Power BI analytics platform. Just in the past several years, RPA vendor Automation Anywhere acquired process discovery and mining startups FortressIQ, Process Gold\\ and StepShot; Blue Prism released a task mining solution called Capture; and rivals including ABBYY and Kryon have expanded their process mining offerings.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/\">Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/embed\/#?secret=wqSRCOP7wQ#?secret=2NKiKfcj0k\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;You know the process space is hot when even Microsoft, with its vast resources, has to buy its way in. I\u2019m sure Microsoft is seeing the same trends that we saw, which drove the combination of FortressIQ and Automation Anywhere,&#8221; Pankaj Chowdhry, EVP of discovery at Automation Anywhere and formerly CEO of FortressIQ, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Customers are starved for process data to help them navigate their transformation journeys and any vendor that doesn&#8217;t have best-in-class process capabilities will find itself challenged to offer a compelling solution to their customers.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft&#8217;s Minit acquisition comes at a time when the broader business process automation industry, which remains <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/robotic-automation-is-back\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flush with cash<\/a>, heads toward general consolidation. SAP acquired German process automation company Signavio in January 2021, just before ServiceNow got into the RPA segment with the buyout of India-based Intellibot.io. IBM <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.ibm.com\/2021-04-15-IBM-to-Acquire-myInvenio-to-help-Organizations-Use-AI-powered-Automation-to-Better-Streamline-Business-Processes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquired<\/a> process mining software company MyInvenio in April. And Salesforce\u2019s MuleSoft and Microsoft followed suit with the purchases of automation tech providers <a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/08\/02\/mulesoft-acquires-rpa-provider-servicetrace\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Servicetrace<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/10\/22\/microsoft-acquires-clear-software-to-strengthen-process-automation-offerings\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clear Software<\/a>, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Process mining, discovery and task mining has seen a lot of transformation with many acquisitions in the last year. [It] now appears to be maturing as a market and becoming commoditized under major automation platforms,&#8221; Saikat Ray, Gartner senior research director, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Gartner sees an emergence of automation platform vendors offering process mining and task mining as embedded capabilities, along with RPA.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated at 4:15 p.m. ET, March 31, with quotes from Microsoft and Automation Anywhere.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired Minit, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which automation","slug":"robotic-process-automation","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449560943"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449560943"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576598619,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/rpa\/","name":"RPA","slug":"rpa","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576598619"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576598619"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":6,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/technology\/","name":"technology","slug":"technology","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/6"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292473,"date":"2022-03-31T14:10:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292473"},"modified":"2022-03-31T14:10:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:57","slug":"better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation\/","title":{"rendered":"Better learning through &#8216;complex dough-manipulation&#8217;"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/robotics-roundup-12\/\">focused on pizza<\/a>. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly straightforward platform onto which ingredients are added.<\/p>\n<p>I say \u201cfairly\u201d here because there are still complications. There\u2019s really no such thing as easy when it comes to building robots that can execute variations on a task at a large scale. Here it\u2019s the dough that presents the problem. Turning a soft and malleable ball of dough into a pizza crust is one of those things humans have figured out how to do efficiently, but it still proves difficult for robot workers.<\/p>\n<p>A team of researchers at MIT, CMU and UC San Diego set out to create what they\u2019ve deemed \u201ccomplex dough-manipulation.\u201d The system is separated into a two-step process, in which the robot must first determine the task and then execute it using a tool like a rolling pin. The system, <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2022\/robotic-deformable-object-0331\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">DiffSkill<\/a>, involves teaching robots complex tasks in simulations.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292473\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>MIT notes:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>A \u201cteacher\u201d algorithm solves each step the robot must take to complete the task. Then, it trains a \u201cstudent\u201d machine-learning model that learns abstract ideas about when and how to execute each skill it needs during the task, like using a rolling pin. With this knowledge, the system reasons about how to execute the skills to complete the entire task.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The researchers say the system outperformed those trained in the more traditional reinforcement learning model. \u201cOur framework provides a novel way for robots to acquire new skills. These skills can then be chained to solve more complex tasks which are beyond the capability of previous robot systems,\u201d says CSAIL grad student, Yunzhu Li.<\/p>\n<p>This is robotics, so the whole pizza thing is really an initial problem for a system designed to tackle a lot more tasks. The company points to the emerging field of eldercare robotics as a possible use going forward.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been focused on pizza. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly Link","children":[]}]},"entities":{"posts":[{"id":2127134,"date":"2021-03-19T09:00:09","date_gmt":"2021-03-19T16:00:09","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2127134"},"modified":"2021-03-19T10:14:17","modified_gmt":"2021-03-19T17:14:17","slug":"ousted-kairos-founder-returns-as-an-advisor-to-the-facial-recognition-startup","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/19\/ousted-kairos-founder-returns-as-an-advisor-to-the-facial-recognition-startup\/","title":{"rendered":"Brian Brackeen returns as an advisor to facial recognition startup Kairos following his ouster as CEO"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Brian Brackeen, the founder and former CEO of facial recognition startup <a href=\"https:\/\/www.kairos.com\/\">Kairos<\/a>, has made his way back to the company following his ouster in 2018. Brackeen is now chairing the company&#8217;s scientific advisory board, where he&#8217;ll help to address and eliminate issues of racial bias from the technology.<\/p>\n<p>While that\u2019s not the company\u2019s explicit mission \u2014 it\u2019s to provide authentication tools to businesses \u2014 algorithmic bias has long been a topic the company, especially Brackeen, has addressed.<\/p>\n<p>But what happened in the time leading up to his ouster and the events that followed was quite the whirlwind.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2127134\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>In 2018, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/10\/27\/facial-recognition-startup-kairos-founder-continues-to-fight-attempted-takeover\/\">Kairos&#8217; board of directors forced Brackeen out of his role as CEO, citing willful misconduct as the cause for his termination<\/a>. In addition to forcing him out of the company he founded, Kairos sued Brackeen, alleging the misappropriation of corporate funds and misleading shareholders.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/10\/27\/facial-recognition-startup-kairos-founder-continues-to-fight-attempted-takeover\/\">At the time<\/a>, Brackeen referred to the events as &#8220;a poorly structured coup,&#8221; and denied the allegations. Then, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/11\/16\/kairos-founder-countersues-for-10-million\/\">Brackeen countersued<\/a> Kairos, alleging the company and its CEO Melissa Doval intentionally destroyed his reputation through fraudulent conduct. In 2019, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/05\/31\/facial-recognition-startup-kairos-settles-lawsuits-with-founder-and-former-ceo-brian-brackeen\/\">Brackeen and Kairos settled the lawsuits.<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/05\/31\/facial-recognition-startup-kairos-settles-lawsuits-with-founder-and-former-ceo-brian-brackeen\/\">Brackeen then went on to start Lightship Capital with his wife, Candice Brackeen<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Since returning to Kairos, Brackeen has already directed Kairos to focus on what it&#8217;s calling the Bias API. The API is designed to make it easier for companies and firms to detect and address any algorithmic biases, according to Brackeen.<\/p>\n<p>Brackeen is not back on a full-time basis, as he has his hands pretty full with Lightship Capital, but he said he&#8217;s generally tasked with steering the ship during quarterly meetings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ckUNckx3h2\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/10\/27\/facial-recognition-startup-kairos-founder-continues-to-fight-attempted-takeover\/\">Facial recognition startup Kairos founder continues to fight attempted takeover<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Facial recognition startup Kairos founder continues to fight attempted takeover&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/10\/27\/facial-recognition-startup-kairos-founder-continues-to-fight-attempted-takeover\/embed\/#?secret=ckUNckx3h2\" data-secret=\"ckUNckx3h2\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Despite the drama of the past, Brackeen told TechCrunch he still considers Kairos to be his baby. It&#8217;s also worth noting that folks like Doval, who was appointed to CEO following Brackeen&#8217;s ouster, and Mary Wolff, the former COO who spearheaded the lawsuit, are gone.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;First, I will always feel a responsibility to the team, investors and fans of Kairos,&#8221; Brackeen said as to why he&#8217;s returned. &#8220;Many of whom I was singularly responsible for. Secondly, as a society, bias can be found in everything from Twitter image cropping to air dryers not turning on for Black hands. It\u2019s a painful reminder of a society that\u2019s not fair for all. The challenge is that as AI gets to be imbedded in more and more products, we will see bias in all kinds of products. Kairos with its large data set and years of IP, must be the firm that saves us from that dystopian future. I am uniquely situated to lead that strategy.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>An earlier version of this post said Stephen Moore is the CEO of Kairos. However, Brackeen has since said Moore has not officially been appointed as CEO of Kairos.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"4vvFYR7v8y\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/17\/to-solve-all-the-small-things-look-to-everyday-little-ai\/\">To solve all the small things, look to everyday Little AI<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;To solve all the small things, look to everyday Little AI&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/17\/to-solve-all-the-small-things-look-to-everyday-little-ai\/embed\/#?secret=4vvFYR7v8y\" data-secret=\"4vvFYR7v8y\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Brian Brackeen, the founder and former CEO of facial recognition startup Kairos, has made his way back to the company following his ouster in 2018. Brackeen is now chairing the company&#8217;s scientific advisory board, where he&#8217;ll help to address and eliminate issues of racial bias from the technology. While that\u2019s not the company\u2019s explicit mission GitHub employee reaches &#8216;amicable resolution&#8217; with company"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">GitHub has reached an &#8220;amicable resolution&#8221; with the person the company fired in the aftermath of the attack on the U.S. Capitol in January, the former employee told TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\">On the day a violent mob of Trump supporters stormed the U.S. Capitol, a worried GitHub employee warned his co-workers in the D.C. area to be safe. After making a comment in Slack saying, \u201cstay safe homies, Nazis are about,\u201d a fellow employee took offense, saying that type of rhetoric wasn\u2019t good for work, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/15\/fired-github-employee-who-warned-coworkers-about-nazis-is-seeking-legal-counsel\/\">the former employee previously told me<\/a>. Two days later, he was fired, with a human relations representative citing a \u201cpattern of behavior that is not conducive to company policy\u201d as the rationale for his termination, he previously told me.<\/p>\n<p>Later that month, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/17\/githubs-head-of-hr-resigns-in-light-of-termination-of-jewish-employee\/\">GitHub COO Erica Brescia said the company\u2019s head of HR took full responsibility for what happened and resigned from the company<\/a>. GitHub did not disclose the name of the person who resigned, but it\u2019s widely known that Carrie Olesen was the chief human resources officer at GitHub. At that time, GitHub said it also &#8220;reversed the decision to separate with the employee\u201d and was talking to his representative.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2125136\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The fired employee, however, did not take his job back.<\/p>\n<div>\u201cWe offered the employee his job back immediately after reviewing the investigation findings, and he declined,\u201d a GitHub spokesperson told TechCrunch.<\/div>\n<p>Instead, he told me, &#8220;Me and the company reached an amicable resolution. I appreciate that they have denounced white supremacy and the dangers it poses to everybody.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>He did not specify the terms of the resolution, but he previously told me he was seeking damages or some other form of reconciliation.<\/p>\n<p>Below is his full statement, which he requested we publish in full:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>Me and the company reached an amicable resolution. I appreciate that they have denounced white supremacy and the dangers it poses to everybody.<\/p>\n<p>We all saw on January 6 that the greatest threat to the USA is not Islam, Black Lives, or defunding police.<\/p>\n<p>White supremacy has us all held hostage using feigned civility, bad-faith arguments\/negotiations, and amtssprache*, and it does not stop until we are all dead or subjugated. I am glad that the nazi coup was a failure, and we avoided a successful Reichstag fire. That said, nazis do not give up easily.<\/p>\n<p>Keep your families and communities safe. Connect with your neighbors and local stores. Fascism and nazism succeed when we are divided. They demand that you abandon reason, that you acquiesce to power and hierarchy, and that you shun altruism. Love yourself. Support, join or create local unions. Build community. Don\u2019t entertain nazis.<\/p>\n<p>I appreciate those who have supported me and my family. I wish you safety and wellness.<\/p>\n<p>Black Lives Matter &amp; Black Power\u00a0<img class=\"CToWUd\" src=\"https:\/\/mail.google.com\/mail\/e\/270a\" alt=\"\u270a\" data-goomoji=\"270a\" data-image-whitelisted=\"\" \/><\/p>\n<p>*Amtssprache<br \/>\n<a href=\"https:\/\/heartlesshypocrisy.com\/what-is-amtssprache\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https:\/\/www.google.com\/url?q=https:\/\/heartlesshypocrisy.com\/what-is-amtssprache\/&amp;source=gmail&amp;ust=1615910980560000&amp;usg=AFQjCNHR3zPC0WenmzhSPvGgVbF495sScQ\">https:\/\/heartlesshypocrisy.<wbr><\/wbr>com\/what-is-amtssprache\/<\/a><\/p>\n<p>Enjoyment &amp; learning for these times<\/p>\n<p>Graphic novels:<br \/>\nMaus<br \/>\nY the Last Man<br \/>\nPulp<br \/>\nSweet Tooth<\/p>\n<p>Songs:<br \/>\n\u201cAlgorhythm\u201d by Childish Gambino<br \/>\n\u201cPlegaria a un Labrador\u201d by Victor Jara<br \/>\n\u201cTweakin\u201d by Vince Staples<br \/>\n\u201cOperation: Mindcrime\u201d by Queensr\u00ffche<\/p>\n<p>Shows:<br \/>\nAvatar Last Airbender &amp; Legend of Korra<br \/>\nAttack on Titan<br \/>\nAtlanta<br \/>\nThe Wire<\/p>\n<p>Books:<br \/>\nGang Leader for a Day by Sudhir Venkatesh<br \/>\nPeople &amp; Permaculture by Looby Macnamara<br \/>\nThe Ways of White Folks by Langston Hughes<br \/>\nPost Traumatic Slave Syndrome by Dr. Joy DeGruy<\/p>\n<p>Movies:<br \/>\nPersepolis<br \/>\nInglorious Basterds<br \/>\nAttack the Block<br \/>\nShawshank Redemption<span style=\"color: #888888;\"><br \/>\n<\/span><\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<hr \/>\n<p><em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/techcrunch-early-stage-is-the-startup-bootcamp-youve-always-needed\/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">Early Stage<\/a> is the premier &#8220;how-to&#8221; event for startup entrepreneurs and investors. "}]}}],"wp:term":[[{"id":35027640,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/diversity-2\/","name":"Diversity","slug":"diversity-2","taxonomy":"category","parent":0,"rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"submenu_categories":[],"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories\/35027640"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=35027640"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=35027640"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=35027640"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":17396,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tc\/","name":"TC","slug":"tc","taxonomy":"category","parent":0,"rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"submenu_categories":[],"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories\/17396"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=17396"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=17396"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=17396"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[{"id":5603054,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/github\/","name":"GitHub","slug":"github","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/5603054"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=5603054"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=5603054"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=5603054"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=5603054"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2123673,"date":"2021-03-10T12:45:22","date_gmt":"2021-03-10T20:45:22","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2123673"},"modified":"2021-03-19T11:20:34","modified_gmt":"2021-03-19T18:20:34","slug":"why-terry-crews-is-launching-a-social-currency","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/10\/why-terry-crews-is-launching-a-social-currency\/","title":{"rendered":"Why Terry Crews is launching a social currency"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Actor Terry Crews is going in on the blockchain. With the help of social currency startup <a href=\"https:\/\/tryroll.com\/\">Roll<\/a>, Crews is launching his own social currency, $POWER.<\/p>\n<p>But first, let&#8217;s break down what that means. Anyone can create a social currency, which hundreds of creators have already done via Roll, to change their relationships with fans and users. Roll enables creators to mint and distribute their own social currency under the <a href=\"https:\/\/www.investopedia.com\/news\/what-erc20-and-what-does-it-mean-ethereum\/\">ERC-20 standard<\/a> and then determine the ways in which their communities can earn and spend that social currency.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Anyone, anywhere, anytime can create their own content,&#8221; Roll founder and CEO Bradley Miles told TechCrunch. &#8220;We refer to this as mass personalization of content. Right now, Roll is experiencing the same thing with money itself. Anyone, anywhere, anytime can create their own money.&#8221;<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2123673\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The way I think of it is it&#8217;s almost like the process for earning and redeeming credit card points but minus the credit card company and plus the blockchain and creators. I haven&#8217;t run this analogy by Miles, but I&#8217;m going with it. Just how your credit card provider gives you points for using your card and then you can redeem those points for cash, airline tickets, etc., creators give fans social currency for engaging with their work in a variety of ways. Then, fans can redeem that social currency for more art, content or what have you.<\/p>\n<p>Currently, there are about 300 creators, including Crews, using Roll. Roll, which has <a href=\"https:\/\/tryroll.com\/roll-fundraise-mainstream\/\">$2.7 million in funding from investors like Balaji Srinivasan, Trevor McFedries and others,<\/a>\u00a0recently saw its <a href=\"https:\/\/app.tryroll.com\/markets\">social currency market cap surpass $1 billion<\/a>. Bradley Miles gifted me .10 $WHALE (worth about $3) so I could get a better understanding of how creators are already using Roll. $WHALE is backed by tangible and rare non-fungible token assets, which means that I can use my $WHALE to buy <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/explosive-inclusive-potential-nfts\/\">NFTs<\/a>. Because Roll enables users to trade their social currency for over 600 other digital assets, that means I could buy the below NFT over on NFT marketplace OpenSea.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2123747\" style=\"width: 1132px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2123747\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2123747 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-10-at-10.47.13-AM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1122\" height=\"616\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-10-at-10.47.13-AM.png 1122w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-10-at-10.47.13-AM.png?resize=150,82 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-10-at-10.47.13-AM.png?resize=300,165 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-10-at-10.47.13-AM.png?resize=768,422 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-10-at-10.47.13-AM.png?resize=680,373 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-10-at-10.47.13-AM.png?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1122px) 100vw, 1122px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2123747\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits: <a href=\"https:\/\/opensea.io\/assets\/0x9e1f3e8db4d1119894624632499eaed1e56d2b1d\/268\">Screenshot\/OpenSea<\/a><\/strong><\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>However, you&#8217;ll see that the Podmork Pix 35 WS cost 28 $WHALE, so I will not be buying this NFT.<\/p>\n<p>In the case of Crews, he envisions folks earning $POWER via blockchain art purchases, NFTs, physical goods and experiences. Initially, Crews is engaging with his $POWER community through Discord. Folks with 50 $POWER, for example, can access a special channel within Discord. To date, Crews had distributed $POWER to about 100 people, he said.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;If I give you $POWER, you own a piece of me,&#8221; Crews said. &#8220;There&#8217;s no other way to put it. And I want to be very careful about who is holding me, no puns intended.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s still early days for $POWER, but Crews says he eventually wants to offer interest-free microloans to artists. The ultimate goal with $POWER is to empower artists.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;That&#8217;s our long-term plan,&#8221; Crews said. &#8220;To become this thing that this community can live and exist in. You could use it anywhere you are &#8212; at Target, the grocery store.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Crews attributes his interest in this space to something that happened to him about four years ago.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"9qH20Dn1ns\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/02\/20\/defi-aims-to-bridge-the-gap-between-blockchains-and-financial-services\/\">DeFi aims to bridge the gap between blockchains and financial services<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;DeFi aims to bridge the gap between blockchains and financial services&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/02\/20\/defi-aims-to-bridge-the-gap-between-blockchains-and-financial-services\/embed\/#?secret=9qH20Dn1ns\" data-secret=\"9qH20Dn1ns\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>While in Milan, Crews said he was trying to buy designer furniture from an artist he respected at <a href=\"https:\/\/www.salonemilano.it\/en\/exhibitions\/international-furnishing-accessories-exhibition\">Salone del Mobile<\/a>. He realized he needed extra money to complete the purchase, but didn&#8217;t have enough cash in his checking account to cover it. So he got on the phone with American Express, he said, who told him to go to a local bank. American Express, on Crews&#8217; behalf, then tried to explain the situation to the local bank manager so that Crews could get the funds he needed to complete the transaction. <span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Crews said the local bank manager took one look at him and said, &#8220;No.&#8221;<\/span><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;And I&#8217;m watching all these white men and women pass me in line, and they&#8217;re looking at me strangely,&#8221; Crews said. &#8220;I&#8217;d been standing there for 15 minutes and it slowly dawns on me that because I&#8217;m Black, I was not going to get my money,&#8221; he said.\u00a0<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">&#8220;That was the moment I knew everything had to change for me.&#8221;<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Crews ended up going to a check-cashing place, in an area where he said his Uber driver refused to go, and got the funds to pay the fees.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Bringing it up still makes me angry,&#8221; he said. &#8220;What I love about this new world of finance is that cryptocurrency does not know what race you are, how old you are.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Through $POWER, Crews hopes to put power back in the hands of artists and creators, Crews explained.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;There&#8217;s no gatekeeper to tell us no,&#8221; he said.<\/p>\n<p>Crews says he&#8217;s also going to start putting out his own content into the $POWER community, where the community will collectively own it together.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;This is bigger than me,&#8221; he said. &#8220;This is a new future.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>For Miles, he envisions a world in which $POWER is accepted at movie theaters or at Paramount Pictures properties.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;[Social currency] is not to replace the dollar,&#8221; Miles said. &#8220;It&#8217;s to complement [money] and do work that probably the dollar is not suited to do.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>I asked Crews if this means he&#8217;s leaving Hollywood and will solely focus on producing his own content for his $POWER community. But Crews said he left Hollywood when he sued William Morris Endeavor in 2017 alleging an executive from the firm groped him. Crews and WME <a href=\"https:\/\/www.washingtonpost.com\/news\/morning-mix\/wp\/2018\/09\/07\/actor-terry-crews-settles-his-lawsuit-against-the-powerful-hollywood-agent-who-allegedly-groped-him\/\">settled the suit in 2018<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;And they were done with me,&#8221; he said. &#8220;But the deal is, is that I had my power. I still had my talent. William Morris threatened to end everything I&#8217;m doing. But everything I&#8217;m doing right now, you can&#8217;t take. So that&#8217;s when I separated from Hollywood. I&#8217;ve never felt like a Hollywood person, even to this day. But every artist out there probably feels the same way. They want their power.&#8221;<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"WcYCNy8Rez\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/explosive-inclusive-potential-nfts\/\">The explosive (and inclusive) potential of NFTs in the creative world<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;The explosive (and inclusive) potential of NFTs in the creative world&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/explosive-inclusive-potential-nfts\/embed\/#?secret=WcYCNy8Rez\" data-secret=\"WcYCNy8Rez\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Actor Terry Crews is going in on the blockchain. It&#8217;s important to have folks on your board who have both the founder&#8217;s and the company&#8217;s best interests in mind, and are able to help the company navigate the many stages of a startup&#8217;s lifecycle.<\/p>\n<p>At <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-early-stage-2021-part-1?promo=boardbuildpost\">TechCrunch&#8217;s Early Stage event<\/a> on April 1 &#8211; 2, Generation Investment Management Partner Dave Easton will talk about board composition, what it takes to make a great board and board governance as a startup scales.<\/p>\n<p>At GIM, Easton has invested in startups like Asana, Andela, Gusto, DocuSign, Toast and others. Meanwhile, he serves on the boards of solar company M-KOPA and has previously served on the boards of Jumia Group and Narayana Health up until their respective initial public offerings.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2121873\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Easton&#8217;s workshop is just one part of a two-day event exploring the many aspects of sure to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-early-stage-2021-part-1?promo=boardbuildpost\">grab your ticket<\/a> to TC Early Stage &#8212; Operations and Fundraising on April 1-2 and save $100 or more when you get the dual-event ticket for both the April and July Early Stage","slug":"techcrunch-early-stage","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576715679"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576715679"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576715679"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576715679"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576715679"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[{"id":576831922,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/event-type\/early-stage\/tc-early-stage-2021-part-1\/","name":"TC Early Stage 2021 - Operations &amp; Fundraising","slug":"tc-early-stage-2021-part-1","taxonomy":"tc_event","rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event\/576831922"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/tc_event"}],"up":[{"embeddable":true,"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event\/576715145"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tc_event=576831922"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_events?tc_event=576831922"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tc_event=576831922"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}]]}},{"id":2121359,"date":"2021-03-08T08:25:28","date_gmt":"2021-03-08T16:25:28","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2121359"},"modified":"2021-03-11T07:13:47","modified_gmt":"2021-03-11T15:13:47","slug":"a-glimpse-inside-the-minds-of-techs-dei-leaders","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/08\/a-glimpse-inside-the-minds-of-techs-dei-leaders\/","title":{"rendered":"A glimpse inside the minds of tech&#8217;s DEI leaders"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Diversity and inclusion as an idea has been on the agenda of tech companies for years now. But the industry still lacks true inclusion, despite best efforts put forth by heads of diversity, equity and inclusion at these companies.<\/p>\n<p>At TC Sessions: Justice, I spoke with Uber Chief Diversity Officer Bo Young Lee and Netflix VP of Inclusion Strategy for Product Wade Davis about the work that still needs to be done, the effects of California&#8217;s Proposition 22 and more.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<h3>On last summer&#8217;s racial justice uprising<\/h3>\n<p>Last summer, after the murder of George Floyd and the subsequent collective consciousness around racial injustice in the U.S., many tech companies spoke out about racism and equality. Davis said he was happy to see more people speaking about those issues but also a bit frustrated that &#8220;it takes something like that for folks to get truly engaged.&#8221;<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2121359\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<blockquote><p><strong>Davis: <\/strong>And inside of Netflix, one of the things that I was really intentional about is to tell our employees who are not Black, right, to not ask our employees how they feel but for them to be much more introspective of what it felt like for them, right, as a white person, or however they identify for them to do the introspection. Because that&#8217;s what it means to be an ally &#8212; to not put the labor on the group that is already feeling the impact and the oppression. And what we found was that many of our employees, for the first time had to wrestle with like, what it means to be white. What it means to be in a situation where you are seeing someone who looks like you take the life of someone who looks like me. So we really tried to switch the actual narrative and the conversation to not add more labor and trauma on our Black employees. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 1:10)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Lee said she was a bit skeptical at the time because we&#8217;ve seen this type of response before in light of the violent killings of Black people.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>Lee: <\/strong>And then within a few weeks you see that interest and that focus wane once more. So I was skeptical that the enthusiasm would continue and enthusiasm in a way to try to solve all of our racism problems in a short period of time. I was surprised that it did continue. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 3:31)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>In her conversations with her counterparts at Uber, Lee said she wanted to make sure that the company didn&#8217;t make such a wide commitment that &#8220;those commitments became nothing more than virtue signaling at the end of the day.&#8221;<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<blockquote><p><strong>Lee: <\/strong>I said to my leadership, if you really want to come out and make some bold statements about being anti-racist, I&#8217;m going to create almost a litmus test to make sure that you really understand what that means because I don&#8217;t want to go up as a company to say we&#8217;re going to be anti-racist and then do nothing about it because that just relives and rehashes the injustices that we&#8217;ve seen in the past. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 4:25)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>So when Uber&#8217;s first post-anti-racism diversity report came out, and it showed Uber&#8217;s Black employee base declined, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/20\/despite-focus-on-anti-racism-ubers-black-employee-base-has-decreased\/\">Lee said at the time that was not acceptable<\/a>.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>Lee: <\/strong>I think part of the commitments we made around being really anti-racist is transparency at all costs, even when we know that transparency could potentially make us look, not reflect as positively on us. So the question did go back, as you know, when we were putting together our diversity report is, &#8216;wow, these numbers are not where we want them to be. None of us are happy about it.&#8217; But in our commitment of being accountable, you know, we want the public to hold us accountable. We want to hold people accountable, we want to be accountable to our workforce, we&#8217;re going to be as transparent about why that decline in black employees happened and underrepresented people happened, what the cause was and what we are doing. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 6:11)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/20\/despite-focus-on-anti-racism-ubers-black-employee-base-has-decreased\/\">Despite commitment to anti-racism, Uber\u2019s Black employee base has decreased<\/a><\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<hr \/>\n<h3><span data-sheets-value=\"{&quot;1&quot;:2,&quot;2&quot;:&quot;&quot;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&quot;2&quot;:12801,&quot;3&quot;:{&quot;1&quot;:0},&quot;12&quot;:0,&quot;15&quot;:&quot;Open Sans&quot;,&quot;16&quot;:12}\">On being early in the DEI journey<\/span><\/h3>\n<p>Netflix, despite having previously reported diversity numbers, only released its <a href=\"https:\/\/about.netflix.com\/en\/news\/netflix-inclusion-report-2021\">first official diversity report this year<\/a>. That&#8217;s partly because the team has only been in place for the last three years, Davis said.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>Davis: <\/strong>So we&#8217;re still at the awareness building phase, like from a foundational standpoint, and we&#8217;re really trying to double down so that folks know why I&amp;D matters. Like, what it actually is, and how it impacts all of us. Because oftentimes, folks think of all of these isms and phobias as something that happens to other people. But if we can really make folks understand that there&#8217;s a cost to all these isms, and phobias to all of us individually, interpersonally, culturally and institutionally, then it makes it easier down the road when folks start to feel somewhat fatigued, right? Because there is always that fatigue factor. So we&#8217;re really trying to get ahead of that. And to have folks to think through like, what is in it for me, and what is in it for my colleagues. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 17:33)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/06\/17\/the-future-of-diversity-and-inclusion-in-tech\/\">The future of diversity and inclusion in tech<\/a><\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<h3>Sharing the DEI load<\/h3>\n<p>Too often does the work of DEI fall on just a handful of people. At Netflix, Davis said it&#8217;s important that there is a shared load, and that all of its leaders are able to speak to the importance of diversity at the company.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>Davis: <\/strong>And I would say our other largest goal is to make sure that all of our leaders can speak to the importance of AI and be more than just a talking point. So how do we build a model that&#8217;s a train the trainer model, where each of our leaders has a one to one inclusion coach, which requires them to have monthly sit-downs with their inclusion partner, where they go on a real intensive journey, so that they can understand how does their leadership style need to evolve and adapt and expand and flex to meet the needs of a larger set of individuals and not the historical ones who folks have engaged with? And we found that to put our leaders on the spot, so that when someone calls me to give a talk, I can say &#8216;No, our COO Greg Peters is just as competent and capable to sit on this panel about inclusion as I am.&#8217; And we feel that we&#8217;re modeling and signaling to our entire organization that this is not just a nice to have, but it&#8217;s part and parcel to your success as an employee, as a leader and to our success as an organization. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 18:26)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"r0Cofc2V9s\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/30\/on-the-diversity-front-2020-may-prove-a-tipping-point\/\">On the diversity front, 2020 may prove a tipping point<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;On the diversity front, 2020 may prove a tipping point&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/30\/on-the-diversity-front-2020-may-prove-a-tipping-point\/embed\/#?secret=r0Cofc2V9s\" data-secret=\"r0Cofc2V9s\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<hr \/>\n<h3>On Prop 22&#8217;s impact on people of color<\/h3>\n<p>Prop 22 went into effect in California earlier this year after a contentious battle where one side, including Uber, Lyft and other tech companies, wanted workers to remain independent contractors and the other side wanted gig workers to be made employees and therefore entitled to more benefits. Prop 22&#8217;s passage was a win for Uber and its counterparts, which collectively spent north of $200 million on its campaign efforts.<\/p>\n<p>Some have wondered how Uber can reconcile its commitment to anti-racism given that many gig workers are people of color. Lee, however, pushed back on that characterization.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>Lee: <\/strong>I would challenge some of those that believe that Prop 22 actually disproportionately hurts people of color. If you actually look at the way the civil rights organizations that came out in support of Prop 22, the NAACP of Northern California and Hawaii came out in support of Prop 22, most of the Hispanic civil rights organizations as well. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 24:59)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Prop 22, of course, was in response to the passage of AB 5, which set new standards of worker classification that were designed to make it harder for companies to classify workers as independent contractors.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>Lee:\u00a0<\/strong>And you looked at the way those exceptions were being made to AB 5, you saw that the exceptions were disproportionately being made for those IC &#8212; you know, independent contractor roles that were predominantly represented by white workers. And they were all getting exceptions from AB 5. And then you look at the roles that were predominantly represented by people of color, especially underrepresented people of color, and those roles were not getting exceptions in AB 5. [&#8230;] For me, how I define racism isn&#8217;t based on intent but it&#8217;s based on impact. And when I see that kind of level of disparate, disproportionate impact, that&#8217;s when I think about, you know, what is racist or not. So I would challenge this notion that [Prop 22] actually disproportionately hurt people of color, especially given that we had civil rights organizations that said we support Prop 22. So, I don&#8217;t think there&#8217;s anything that really needs to be reconciled, from my perspective and from the organization&#8217;s perspective.\u00a0<em><strong>(Timestamp: 24:59)<\/strong><\/em><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/03\/ca-supreme-court-denies-lawsuit-challenging-prop-22s-constitutionality\/\">CA Supreme Court denies lawsuit challenging Prop 22\u2019s constitutionality<\/a><\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/15\/uber-lobbies-for-prop-22-style-gig-work-standards-in-the-eu\/\">Uber lobbies for \u2018Prop 22\u2019-style gig work standards in the EU<\/a><\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/13\/an-even-bigger-battle-for-gig-worker-rights-is-on-the-horizon\/\">An even bigger battle for gig worker rights is on the horizon<\/a><\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&quot;1&quot;:2,&quot;2&quot;:&quot;&quot;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&quot;2&quot;:12801,&quot;3&quot;:{&quot;1&quot;:0},&quot;12&quot;:0,&quot;15&quot;:&quot;Open Sans&quot;,&quot;16&quot;:12}\"> <div embedded-video-placeholder=\"60400dc3303d501d18141bbc\" post-id=\"2120707\"><\/div> <\/span><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/otter.ai\/u\/zN--5q60dfqViVw9Tfh4fJwG0as\">You can read the entire transcript here<\/a>.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p><em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/techcrunch-early-stage-is-the-startup-bootcamp-youve-always-needed\/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">Early Stage<\/a> is the premier &#8220;how-to&#8221; event for startup entrepreneurs and investors. You\u2019ll hear firsthand how some of the most successful founders and VCs build their businesses, raise money and manage their portfolios. We\u2019ll cover every aspect of company building: Fundraising, recruiting, sales, product-market fit, PR, marketing and brand building. Each session also has audience participation built-in &#8212; there\u2019s ample time included for audience questions and discussion.<\/em><\/p>\n<p>\t<iframe\n\t\t\tid=\"wpcom-iframe-dde292b93a5f3017145419dd51bb9fce\"\n\t\t\twidth=\"99%\"\n\t\t\theight=\"1500\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https:\/\/tcprotectedembed.com\/protected-iframe\/dde292b93a5f3017145419dd51bb9fce\"\n\t\t\tscrolling=\"true\"\n\t\t\tframeborder=\"0\"\n\t\t\tclass=\"wpcom-protected-iframe\"\n\t>\n\t<\/iframe>\n\t<script
