Davis","slug":"wade-davis","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576862034"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576862034"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576862034"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576862034"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576862034"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[{"id":576821871,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/event-type\/sessions\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/","name":"TC Sessions: Justice 2021","slug":"tc-sessions-justice-2021","taxonomy":"tc_event","rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event\/576821871"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/tc_event"}],"up":[{"embeddable":true,"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event\/449559507"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tc_event=576821871"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_events?tc_event=576821871"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tc_event=576821871"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}]]}},{"id":2119188,"date":"2021-03-08T07:30:05","date_gmt":"2021-03-08T15:30:05","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2119188"},"modified":"2021-03-11T07:10:57","modified_gmt":"2021-03-11T15:10:57","slug":"the-path-forward-for-essential-workers","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/08\/the-path-forward-for-essential-workers\/","title":{"rendered":"The path forward for essential workers"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Gig workers and<\/span> warehouse workers have become essential in a pandemic-ravaged economy. In California, a law went into effect earlier this year that makes gig workers independent contractors. Meanwhile, Amazon warehouse workers in Alabama are actively seeking to form a union to ensure better protections at the workplace.<\/p>\n<p>At TC Sessions: Justice, I spoke with Gig Workers Collective co-founder and organizer Vanessa Bain, The Congress of Essential Workers founder and former Amazon warehouse worker Christian Smalls and National Council for Occupational Safety and Health Co-Executive Director Jessica E. Martinez about what\u2019s next for gig workers and tech\u2019s contractor workforce, and what battles lie ahead for these essential workers.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<h3>On the Amazon union drive<\/h3>\n<p>Amazon warehouse workers in Bessemer, Alabama are in the midst of a <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/07\/amazon-warehouse-workers-begin-historic-vote-to-unionize\/\">historic union drive<\/a>. Smalls, who was fired from his job at an Amazon warehouse in Staten Island last year after speaking out about the lack of personal protective equipment, told me he recently spent a few days in Bessemer.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2119188\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<blockquote><p>The building opened up when coronavirus started. When New York City became the epicenter, that&#8217;s when the Bessemer facility opened up. So the union got a head start on talking to workers. So that&#8217;s a gem for anybody or any union that plans on trying to unionize the building &#8212; that you have a facility in your community that&#8217;s about to open up, when opening, that&#8217;s the best time to connect with workers. That&#8217;s what happened last year. And as a result, the workers had seen what happened to the workers that were unprotected and they don&#8217;t want that. They want better for themselves. And they rightfully deserve that, especially in Alabama. It&#8217;s a right to work state, a state with no state minimum, obviously a red state. So I think it&#8217;s a lot of intangibles against them. But these workers now see the window of opportunity for change systemically. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 4:40)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Meanwhile, President Biden recently came out in support of the unionizing efforts in Bessemer.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>I would hope that he is a man of his word. He&#8217;s a pro-union guy. He ran his campaign off of that, saying he&#8217;s a union guy and unions need to be strong, and he supports unions all the way. It was powerful to see that the president, the man, the highest plateau in the country, supports the union. <em><strong>(Timestamp: 13:11)<\/strong><\/em><\/p>\n<p>[&#8230;] But once again, like Vanessa said, I don&#8217;t put all my eggs in that basket either. I just want to hold him accountable. Make sure that, you know, we see this all the way through to the end. Even if Alabama is not successful, if we were to try again, in other locations, other parts of the country, that we have the support of the highest power in the country, that is the most powerful thing that will resonate with workers. So it&#8217;s good to see that it&#8217;s happening now. <em><strong>(Timestamp: 14:17)<\/strong><\/em><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/07\/amazon-warehouse-workers-begin-historic-vote-to-unionize\/\">Amazon warehouse workers to begin historic vote to unionize<\/a><\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/12\/amazon-faces-lawsuit-alleging-failure-to-provide-ppe-to-workers-during-pandemic\/\">Amazon faces lawsuit alleging failure to provide PPE to workers during pandemic<\/a><\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/17\/amazon-ny-ag-lawsuit\/\">NY AG sues Amazon over treatment of warehouse workers<\/a><\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<hr \/>\n<h3>On the effects of Prop 22<\/h3>\n<p>Already, Prop 22 has affected industries outside of tech. In December, supermarket chain Albertsons began replacing delivery drivers with contractors and hundreds of employees in California were swapped for DoorDash workers, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/features\/2021-02-17\/gig-economy-coming-for-millions-of-u-s-jobs-after-california-s-uber-lyft-vote?sref=gni836kR\">Bloomberg reported<\/a>. Meanwhile, tech companies have spoken about implementing Prop 22-like legislation in other parts of the country. Martinez described how some California residents who voted to pass Prop 22 thought they were supporting workers for better access to rights.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>And unfortunately, you have workers who have possibly died. We have a California rideshare driver who died from COVID-19 last month. His independent classification means his family will receive no workers&#8217; compensation. That is a huge impact to workers and the reality of how it impacts day to day life for workers and in the midst of a pandemic. So I share that, because Prop 22 sets the tone, again, for what could happen nationally.\u00a0<strong><em>(Timestamp: 17:00)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Meanwhile, Bain said she sees the passing of Prop 22 as a failure of &#8220;our entire structure of economy.&#8221;<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>And we have really allowed tech to run rampant under this pretense that somehow it&#8217;s innovative, and especially within the gig economy. I mean, it&#8217;s the opposite of innovative, right? Like it&#8217;s feudalism on your phone, right? It&#8217;s 1-800 dial listserv. So it&#8217;s like, they&#8217;re not doing anything new that justifies creating an entirely different classification of labor than existed before, which is what Prop 22 did, right? It literally created this category of marketplace contractor that retains neither the protections of an independent contractor nor an employee. And allowing, you know, companies to write their own laws in this way is a systemic failure. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 18:57)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/13\/an-even-bigger-battle-for-gig-worker-rights-is-on-the-horizon\/\">An even bigger battle for gig worker rights is on the horizon<\/a><\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/05\/gig-workers-survey-san-francisco\/\">Gig workers in San Francisco are mostly people of color and many are immigrants, according to survey<\/a><\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/16\/ex-postmates-vp-of-global-public-policy-on-the-future-of-gig-work\/\">Ex-Postmates VP of global public policy on the future of gig work<\/a><\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<hr \/>\n<h3>On the PRO Act<\/h3>\n<p>There&#8217;s legislation in the U.S. Senate right now that aims to make it easier for workers to organize and form unions in the country. The Protecting the Right to Organize Act seeks to change labor laws in favor of giving workers more power.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"NCi7T15Ei2\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/07\/24\/tech-at-work-black-gig-workers-speak-out-and-a-look-at-uber-commitment-to-being-anti-racist-and-facebooks-diversity-report\/\">Black gig workers speak out, Uber&#8217;s commitment to being anti-racist and Facebook&#8217;s diversity report<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Black gig workers speak out, Uber&#8217;s commitment to being anti-racist and Facebook&#8217;s diversity report&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/07\/24\/tech-at-work-black-gig-workers-speak-out-and-a-look-at-uber-commitment-to-being-anti-racist-and-facebooks-diversity-report\/embed\/#?secret=NCi7T15Ei2\" data-secret=\"NCi7T15Ei2\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Bain spoke about the importance of getting the PRO Act across the line in light of the passing of Prop 22 in California.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>These things shouldn&#8217;t be at the mercy of who happens to be, you know, held to a position. These are things that should be codified and enshrined really in law. And things that should be consistent and stable protections that people can rely on and count on.\u00a0<strong><em>(Timestamp: 20:22)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Martinez explained how the PRO Act aligns with the <a href=\"https:\/\/nationalcosh.org\/sites\/default\/files\/2021-02%20National%20Agenda%20for%20Worker%20Safety%20and%20Health.pdf\">work she&#8217;s doing at COSH<\/a>. The organization recently released a national agenda for worker safety and health, along with some recommendations.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>We want stronger safety laws, tougher enforcement, including a mandatory emergency standard to prevent the spread of infectious disease. And again, this is federally so if there is an ETS or an emergency [temporary] standard pass, it applies all over and impacts all kinds of workers, stronger protections against retaliation.\u00a0<strong><em>(Timestamp: 07:53)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Martinez added:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>Employers will funnel resources to try scare tactics to scare workers from organizing, demanding safer workplaces, job security, and so forth. [The agenda] also includes workers are included in all policy decisions. We believe strongly that workers, more than anyone, understand the job, know the solutions and controls to health and safety issues, and also equity and inclusion to end the misclassification and better protections for temporary gig workers. Paid sick and family leave for workers, also worker centered health protocols, including health for high-risk workers and getting access to vaccines. And we want to confront the workplace effects of climate change. Finally, also prevent chemical catastrophes and harmful exposure. [&#8230;] With that said, this is not working in isolation. It works in collaboration with laws, we&#8217;re hoping that will pass, such as the PRO Act, allowing workers to gain bargaining power when organizing, essentially giving them the ability to negotiate with the employer to get access to benefits again, such as some job security paid sick leave, workers comp and so forth. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 8:23)<\/em><\/strong><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&quot;1&quot;:2,&quot;2&quot;:&quot;&quot;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&quot;2&quot;:12801,&quot;3&quot;:{&quot;1&quot;:0},&quot;12&quot;:0,&quot;15&quot;:&quot;Open Sans&quot;,&quot;16&quot;:12}\"> <div embedded-video-placeholder=\"603fd6c1fb2e1e3363ff491c\" post-id=\"2120505\"><\/div> <\/span><\/p>\n<p>You can read the <a href=\"https:\/\/otter.ai\/u\/UGTB23Mu9JiPv-cYY5YHKQ3IZOA\">entire transcript here<\/a>.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p><em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/techcrunch-early-stage-is-the-startup-bootcamp-youve-always-needed\/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">Early Stage<\/a> is the premier &#8220;how-to&#8221; event for startup entrepreneurs and investors. You\u2019ll hear firsthand how some of the most successful founders and VCs build their businesses, raise money and manage their portfolios. We\u2019ll cover every aspect of company building: Fundraising, recruiting, sales, product-market fit, PR, marketing and brand building. Each session also has audience participation built-in &#8212; there\u2019s ample time included for audience questions and discussion.<\/em><\/p>\n<p>\t<iframe\n\t\t\tid=\"wpcom-iframe-dde292b93a5f3017145419dd51bb9fce\"\n\t\t\twidth=\"99%\"\n\t\t\theight=\"1500\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https:\/\/tcprotectedembed.com\/protected-iframe\/dde292b93a5f3017145419dd51bb9fce\"\n\t\t\tscrolling=\"true\"\n\t\t\tframeborder=\"0\"\n\t\t\tclass=\"wpcom-protected-iframe\"\n\t>\n\t<\/iframe>\n\t<script Sessions: Justice 2021","slug":"tc-sessions-justice-2021","taxonomy":"tc_event","rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event\/576821871"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/tc_event"}],"up":[{"embeddable":true,"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event\/449559507"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tc_event=576821871"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_events?tc_event=576821871"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tc_event=576821871"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}]]}},{"id":2118455,"date":"2021-03-02T14:25:16","date_gmt":"2021-03-02T22:25:16","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2118455"},"modified":"2021-03-12T15:00:38","modified_gmt":"2021-03-12T23:00:38","slug":"explosive-inclusive-potential-nfts","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/explosive-inclusive-potential-nfts\/","title":{"rendered":"The explosive (and inclusive) potential of NFTs in the creative world"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Digital collectibles are<\/span> having a very large moment. Just last month, a piece of digital art by Beeple sold for $6.6 million on online art marketplace <a href=\"https:\/\/niftygateway.com\/\">Nifty Gateway.<\/a> Meanwhile, Linkin Park&#8217;s Mike Shinoda recently sold clips of a song <a href=\"https:\/\/www.inputmag.com\/culture\/linkin-park-mike-shinoda-happy-endings-nft-interview\">via online marketplace Zora<\/a>. Over on Dapper Labs&#8217; NBA Top Shot, more than 200,000 people recently waited hours for the chance to buy one of just 10,631 packs of digital NBA moments.<\/p>\n<p>Those marketplaces, along with others, are where people go to buy digital assets, or, non-fungible tokens (NFTs) that live on the blockchain. This whole world of NFTs is super new to me (I&#8217;ve only been using Top Shot for a couple of weeks now) so I caught up with a couple of NFT creators to break it down for me, as well as share some insights on where they think the space is going, and its overall potential.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The way I like to explain NFTs, they are digital assets with true ownership and provenance,&#8221; <a href=\"https:\/\/makersplace.com\/richardrivera\/\">Ronin the Collector <\/a>told TechCrunch. &#8220;You can track their origin and they can only be owned by one person.&#8221;<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2118455\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Many people, myself included, at some point wonder why someone would pay for a short video clip of, for example, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nbatopshot.com\/moment\/mrd+ee07ddae-7658-4c39-93ca-b01643e0e814?\">Stephen Curry making a three-pointer<\/a> when you download it to your computer for free.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Humans inherently, whether we will like to admit it or not, want to own things,&#8221; Ronin said. &#8220;And I think that that&#8217;s part of the human experience is owning things. When you own things, it&#8217;s a connection, and it&#8217;s like you have reason for being and there&#8217;s something unique about ownership. And I think that at the end of the day, yeah, you can you can watch it all you want. But can you sell it?&#8221;<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">This is the one! All the \ud83d\udd25\ud83d\udd25\ud83d\udd25 \u2066<a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/nba_topshot?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@nba_topshot<\/a>\u2069 <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/KBFsTK1IIs\">https:\/\/t.co\/KBFsTK1IIs<\/a>?<\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Big Italy (@BigItaly42) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/BigItaly42\/status\/1365357499105357831?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">February 26, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>With that clip as an NFT, you can. As an example, one user bought a LeBron James dunk for $208,000 a couple of weeks ago, <a href=\"https:\/\/cryptoslam.io\/nba-top-shot\/sales\">according to CryptoSlam<\/a>. <a href=\"https:\/\/blog.nbatopshot.com\/posts\/state-of-nba-topshot?utm_source=Twitter&amp;utm_medium=organic&amp;utm_campaign=stateofnbatopshot_blog\">Last month<\/a>, Top Shot reached nearly $50 million in marketplace transactions. Then, over a 24-hour period last week, Top Shot saw more than $37 million in sales, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cryptoslam.io\/nba-top-shot\">according to Cryptoslam<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>As to why they&#8217;re blowing up right now, Ronin attributes it to a couple of things: the pandemic that&#8217;s forced everyone behind a computer screen and an easy entry point. Top Shot, for example, makes it super easy for plebeians like me to sign up and you don&#8217;t need to have a crypto wallet. You can just use your credit card. The same goes for Nifty Gateway.<\/p>\n<p>But Top Shot and Nifty are outliers, Ronin said. For the majority of NFT platforms, you need to have an Ethereum wallet. As Cooper Turley, crypto strategy lead at Audius, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/27\/if-you-havent-followed-nfts-heres-why-you-should-start\/\">wrote on TC<\/a>, &#8220;this means collectors need to purchase ETH from an exchange like Coinbase and send it to a non-custodial address that consists of a long string of numbers and letters to get started.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>That sounds like a whole thing that I, for one, am not ready to dive into. In general, barriers to access continue to be a problem in the NFTs space, Ronin said.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Projects are just now starting to pay attention to the user experience,&#8221; he said. &#8220;And just barely in time. One of the best rooms I&#8217;ve been on Clubhouse was one that talked about how basically, with the whole world watching, how do we not mess this up. So I think when you have a product like Top Shot, which is easy to get into, easy to sign up for, and easy to purchase. You have to use a credit card, you don&#8217;t need crypto and throw in the mix that everyone&#8217;s online and then <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2021\/02\/24\/arts\/design\/christies-beeple-auction-blockchain-art.html\">Beeple sells $3 million worth of digital art<\/a>, and all of a sudden, people want to pay attention. So I think that was the catalyst.&#8221;<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p>But an even more expansive and interesting arena for NFTs than Top Shot is the world of NFT art. <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/sirsuhayb\">Ameer Carter<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/iamsirsu.com\/cryptomedia\">an artist<\/a> that is also known as Sirsu, got into NFTs last summer thanks to a friend, he told TechCrunch. Pretty much immediately, he said, he realized the transformative nature of the technology.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We literally have creative immortality,&#8221; he told me he realized at the time.<\/p>\n<p>But the art world has historically been inhospitable to Black folks and people of color, and especially in the world of NFTs, Carter said. The traditional art scene, Carter said, is elitist. And while Carter himself is a classically trained artist, he hasn&#8217;t been able to make his way into the traditional art world, he said.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;And it&#8217;s not because of lack of trying,&#8221; he said.<\/p>\n<p>Carter said he&#8217;s had a number of conversations with art curators who all love his work, but they&#8217;ve told him it&#8217;s not &#8220;something that they could build a whole curriculum around and intellectualize,&#8221; he said. What NFTs do is enable artists like Carter to create and share their art in a way that hadn&#8217;t previously been afforded to them.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">SIRSU Trading Card Series, &quot;Androinomicon&quot; explores themes of human nature through alliteration and android motifs. <\/p>\n<p>Pack two: Pile \/ Push \/ Pull.<br \/>27 remaining! <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/XwmA04W01J\">pic.twitter.com\/XwmA04W01J<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; (vain) sirsu.eth (@sirsuhayb) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/sirsuhayb\/status\/1354304148259409921?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">January 27, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;And this is a much more open and accessible platform, and environment for them to do so,&#8221; Carter said. &#8220;And so my goal is to help really give them that type of visibility and empower them to be creatives. My mission is to remove the starving artists stigma. I don&#8217;t believe that creativity is cheap. I believe that it is rich. And it enriches and it gives us the reasons why we live in the first place.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>However, Carter said he&#8217;s begun to notice white folks taking credit for things Black artists have already done.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;There&#8217;s this push and pull between folks who are really about the provenance of the blockchain versus folks who are wanting to predispose themselves as first because they have more visibility,&#8221; Carter said.<\/p>\n<p>He pointed to Black artists like <a href=\"https:\/\/danky.art\/portfolio\">Connie Digital<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/app.rarible.com\/harrisonfirst\">Harrison First<\/a> and others who were some of the first people to institute social tokens for their fans on the blockchain.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;They were some of the first to deploy and sell albums as NFTs, EPs as NFTs, singular songs,&#8221; Carter said. &#8220;And now we have <a href=\"https:\/\/www.globenewswire.com\/news-release\/2021\/02\/17\/2177446\/0\/en\/Acclaimed-Musician-3LAU-Launches-First-NFT-Album-on-Origin-s-Dshop.html\">Blau<\/a> that came out and people were saying he&#8217;s the first to sell an album. And it&#8217;s like, well, that&#8217;s not true, technically. But what works and has continued to work is because there&#8217;s a lot of hoopla and a lot of money around that sale, that becomes the formative thing as being first because it&#8217;s the one that&#8217;s made the most noise. And I find it interesting because of the fact that we can literally go back tangibly, and there&#8217;s verifiable hash proof that it wasn&#8217;t the case.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>These are the types of phenomena pushing Carter to become an NFT archivist of sorts, he said.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I&#8217;m not necessarily a historian, but I think the more and more I get involved in this space, the more and more I feel that pressing role of being an archivist,&#8221; he said. &#8220;So that culturally, we aren&#8217;t erased, even in a space that&#8217;s supposed to be decentralized and supposed to be something that works for everyone.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>That&#8217;s partly why Carter is building The Well to archive the work of Black artists, like <a href=\"https:\/\/linktr.ee\/blacksneakers\">Blacksneakers<\/a>, for example. The Well will also be a platform for Black artists to mint their NFTs in a place that feels safe, supportive and not exploitative, he said.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2119426\" style=\"width: 1235px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2119426\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2119426 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/02\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-01-at-5.25.17-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1225\" height=\"656\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/02\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-01-at-5.25.17-PM.png 1225w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/02\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-01-at-5.25.17-PM.png?resize=150,80 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/02\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-01-at-5.25.17-PM.png?resize=300,161 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/02\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-01-at-5.25.17-PM.png?resize=768,411 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/02\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-01-at-5.25.17-PM.png?resize=680,364 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/02\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-01-at-5.25.17-PM.png?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1225px) 100vw, 1225px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2119426\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> <a href=\"https:\/\/superrare.co\/artwork-v2\/in-the-summer,-i-wish-to-be-with-you-13409\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Black Sneakers via SuperRare <span class=\"screen-reader-text\">(opens in a new window)<\/span><\/a><\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>On current platforms, Carter said it feels like white artists generally get more promotions on the site, as well as on social media, than Black artists.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;They deserve to have that kind of artists&#8217; growth and development,&#8221; Carter said. &#8220;Yet it is afforded to a lot of other artists that don&#8217;t look like them.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Carter said he recognizes it&#8217;s not the responsibility of platforms like Nifty Gateway, SuperRare and others to provide opportunities to Black artists, but that they do have the ability to put Black artists in a better position to receive opportunities.<\/p>\n<p>That&#8217;s partly what Carter hopes to achieve with <a href=\"https:\/\/ownthewell.com\/\">The Well Protocol.<\/a> The Well, which Carter plans to launch on Juneteenth, aims to create an inclusive platform and ecosystem for NFT artists, collectors and curators. Carter said he wants artists to not have to feel like they have to constantly leverage Twitter to showcase their work. Instead, they&#8217;ll have the full backing of an ecosystem pumping up their work.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Everywhere else, you look at other artists and they have write-ups, and they have news coverage and things of that nature,&#8221; Carter said. &#8220;And [Black artists] don&#8217;t have a lot of those avenues to compete. You know, I&#8217;m in the business of building true equity for us, so part and parcel to that is developing the tools and the ecosystem for us to thrive.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>No longer should art just be for the rich, Carter said.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We have the ability to completely dismantle that,&#8221; he said. &#8220;So we have to be very, very, very careful about that and make a concerted effort to make that thing work, but we can&#8217;t do it when we have folks entering the space with money erasing folks who were already here. We can&#8217;t have that where platforms are not allowing the positioning of artists to grow. You know, we can&#8217;t have that when we have folks by and large, fear mongering and trying to get other artists to not be a part of this system.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s also important, he said, for NFTs to not solely be seen as collectible, investable objects.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Everyone&#8217;s getting into the game like it&#8217;s a money grab,&#8221; he said. &#8220;It&#8217;s not. It&#8217;s playing with artists lives and careers here.&#8221;<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p>For those who aren&#8217;t yet in on NFTs, there&#8217;s still time, Ronin said. Even with the increased attention on NFTs, Ronin says it&#8217;s still early days.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Honestly, I don&#8217;t even think we&#8217;ve got a full foot into early adoption yet,&#8221; he said. &#8220;I don&#8217;t think you come out of early adoption until we&#8217;ve got a solid experience across the board. I think we&#8217;re still in alpha.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>That&#8217;s partly because Ronin believes the things people will be able to do in five or ten years with this technology will pale in comparison to what&#8217;s happening today. For example, Ronin said he spoke with an artist who is experimenting with an NFT experience that will transcend VR, AR and XR.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;And I&#8217;m so excited that she chose to work with me and bring me in on this, and use me as kind of an advisor,&#8221; he said. &#8220;And she can change the world with this technology.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>That&#8217;s really what&#8217;s so exciting about NFTs for Ronin &#8212; the notion that the technology can change your life, and the world, he said.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;And it is a space in which you should feel free to come into and dream big and then figure out how to make those dreams happen,&#8221; he said. &#8220;You can use AR, VR, mobile, you know, the internet &#8212; you can use all these aspects and create an NFT experience that transcends space, transcends time, transcends our life. So it&#8217;s a super powerful technology. And I think that people should really pay attention.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Down the road, Ronin also envisions having connected blockchains &#8220;where you can take an NFT from, you know, Bitcoin to Ethereum to <a href=\"https:\/\/on.wax.io\/wax-io\/\">WAX<\/a> to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.onflow.org\/\">Flow,<\/a>&#8221; he said. &#8220;I really think that it&#8217;s why this this is that important.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>For Carter, he hopes his work at The Well will help to set a precedent for inclusivity and access in the NFT space. It&#8217;s worth mentioning that Carter is also working on the <a href=\"https:\/\/mint.af\/\">Mint Fund<\/a> to help minimize the barriers to entry for artists looking to mint their first NFTs. Minting an NFT can be expensive to the tune of $50-$250 depending on how busy the Ethereum network is, and Mint Fund will pay those fees for new artists, making the on-ramp into the world smoother.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;If we don&#8217;t do this the right way with the right type of community-driven thinking, then we will lose,&#8221; he said. &#8220;And it&#8217;s not going to look good, it&#8217;s going to be ugly. And it&#8217;s going to again perpetuate the rich getting richer and the poor getting poorer&#8230;We have to find the best ways to redistribute wealth at any given point in time within this economy, within this system. If we do not know how to do that, we are fucked. At least in my opinion.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>There are also conversations in the space around the <a href=\"https:\/\/www.loop-news.com\/p\/the-big-problem-with-nfts-energy\">ecological impact of minting NFTs<\/a>, which requires a good amount of energy to do. Carter described the existence of two camps: the camp arguing minting NFTs are very ecologically damaging and the ones saying it&#8217;s not the fault of minters and you can&#8217;t blame them &#8220;for minting on a system that is already going to process these transactions, whether they mint or not.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>For Carter, he thinks the first camp could be right, but says there&#8217;s just a lot of yelling at this point.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I think that collectively, us as minters should not feel so fucked up that we can&#8217;t do anything anymore,&#8221; he said.<\/p>\n<p>Carter also pointed to the energy required to print and ship a bunch of his work.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;To sell one piece of art that I&#8217;ve minted versus the energy expenditure and the emissions it takes for me to sell, let&#8217;s say 1,000 prints at $20,&#8221; he said. &#8220;To now shop those to 1,000 different places and for those things to then be transported to 1,000 different homes. Like, maybe they&#8217;re comparable, maybe they&#8217;re not. I&#8217;m not too interested in doing the math at this point.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Ultimately, Carter thinks there needs to be better access to renewable energy sources and more innovative hardware in the space.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;And the production of creating that innovative hardware also has to be coming from renewable energy sources, like the entire framework should be working to be carbon negative,&#8221; he said. &#8220;As carbon neutral to carbon negative as possible. And not just the minting side but the mining side. And, you know, the manufacturing side. It&#8217;s a cyclical issue.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Digital collectibles are having a very large moment. Just last month, a piece of digital art by Beeple sold for $6.6 million on online art marketplace Nifty Gateway. Meanwhile, Linkin Park&#8217;s Mike Shinoda recently sold clips of a song via online marketplace Zora. Over on Dapper Labs&#8217; NBA Top Shot, more than 200,000 people recently ion-tomorrow-at-tc-sessions-justice\/","title":{"rendered":"Hear from Uber, Facebook and Netflix about diversity, equity and inclusion at TC Sessions: Justice"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Tech companies are no stranger to controversy and workplace issues. Over the years, it&#8217;s become clear that no company is immune from diversity issues. But it&#8217;s the job of those in the diversity, equity and inclusion departments to create and foster environments that are welcoming to all.<\/p>\n<p>Last year, in the wake of the police killings of George Floyd, Breonna Taylor and others, many companies spoke out in support of Black lives and the Black Lives Matter movement. At <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/?utm_medium=editpost&amp;utm_campaign=justice2021&amp;utm_content=arlanhamilton&amp;utm_source=tc&amp;promo=uberfbnetflixpost&amp;display=TRUE\">TechCrunch Sessions: Justice<\/a>, we&#8217;ll examine what some companies said at the time and how those statements align with where they are today.<\/p>\n<p>We&#8217;ll also dive in to the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/14\/examining-the-pipeline-problem\/\">myth of the pipeline problem,<\/a> as well as the idea of imposter syndrome and <a href=\"https:\/\/hbr.org\/2021\/02\/stop-telling-women-they-have-imposter-syndrome\">how companies can help<\/a> to shift the onus from the person experiencing feelings of doubt to the systems and cultures that perpetuate biases, sexism and racism. We&#8217;ll also, of course, talk about each company&#8217;s DEI efforts over the years, where progress has been made and where there&#8217;s still room for improvement.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2117552\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>To have this conversation, we&#8217;ve called on three DEI leaders from Uber, Facebook and Netflix to share their experiences, struggles and wins leading the charge for genuine inclusivity in tech.<\/p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s a bit about the three of them:<\/p>\n<p><strong>Bo Young Lee, Uber Chief Diversity Officer<\/strong><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1712901\" style=\"width: 643px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1712901\" loading=\"lazy\" https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/09\/42731328210_3aea5d73cd_k.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/09\/42731328210_3aea5d73cd_k.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/09\/42731328210_3aea5d73cd_k.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/09\/42731328210_3aea5d73cd_k.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 633px) 100vw, 633px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1712901\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Photo by Kimberly White\/Getty Images for TechCrunch \/ Getty Images<\/p><\/div><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Lee became <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/01\/23\/uber-has-hired-a-chief-diversity-officer\/\">Uber&#8217;s first-ever chief diversity officer in early 2018<\/a>. Lee joined about one year after <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/06\/11\/ubers-board-votes-unanimously-to-adopt-all-recommendations-of-holder-report\/?_ga=2.229786132.962186928.1614100640-1057749772.1591641289\">former U.S. Attorney General Eric Holder and his law firm recommended<\/a> Uber have a chief diversity officer. Holder and his firm were tapped in the aftermath of former Uber engineer Susan Fowler&#8217;s allegations of sexual harassment at the company.<\/p>\n<p>At TC Sessions: Justice, I&#8217;ll chat with Lee about where Uber is today, as well as how it is doing in its mission to double Black representation in leadership by 2025.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Sandra Altine, VP of Workforce Diversity and Inclusion\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2116848\" style=\"width: 544px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2116848\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2116848 \" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"534\" height=\"534\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg 1800w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?resize=768,768 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?resize=680,680 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?resize=1536,1536 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Sandra-Altine.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 534px) 100vw, 534px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2116848\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">(Photo courtesy of Facebook)<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Altine joined Facebook last April after previously serving as the managing director of global diversity and inclusion for investor service Moody&#8217;s.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/07\/10\/tech-at-work-dei-at-facebook-prop-22-and-gig-worker-earnings\/\">Last year<\/a>, Facebook committed to having 50% of its workforce be members of underrepresented groups, which includes BIPOC, women, disabled people and veterans. Over the next five years, Facebook also said it\u2019s committed to increasing its Black employee base by 30%; currently 3.8% of its U.S.-based employees are Black.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Wade Davis, VP of Inclusion Strategy for Product<\/strong><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2110931\" style=\"width: 523px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2110931\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2110931 \" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"513\" height=\"513\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg 1800w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?resize=768,768 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?resize=680,680 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?resize=1536,1536 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/Wade-Davis.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 513px) 100vw, 513px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2110931\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Photo courtesy of Netflix<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Davis, who joined Netflix in this role in September 2019, works directly with product leaders at the company to implement inclusive policies and practices into the workplaces. He also works alongside other VPs at Netflix to improve upon diversity and inclusion within the workforce. Prior to joining Netflix, Davis consulted for Google, P&amp;G and others.<\/p>\n<p>Netflix released its <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/netflix-releases-latest-diversity-numbers\/\">first-ever diversity report just this year<\/a>. Netflix had previously disclosed its data but had yet to make a full report out of it. Netflix did not lay out any concrete goals, but said it\u2019s generally wanting to increase representation by hiring more inclusively and building out its recruiting networks.<\/p>\n<p>Be sure to Justice","slug":"sessions-justice","taxonomy":"tc_event","rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event\/449559666"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/tc_event"}],"up":[{"embeddable":true,"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_event\/449559507"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tc_event=449559666"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_events?tc_event=449559666"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tc_event=449559666"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}]]}},{"id":2117388,"date":"2021-02-24T10:48:26","date_gmt":"2021-02-24T18:48:26","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2117388"},"modified":"2021-02-24T16:48:26","modified_gmt":"2021-02-25T00:48:26","slug":"kapor-capital-is-raising-a-125-million-fund","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/24\/kapor-capital-is-raising-a-125-million-fund\/","title":{"rendered":"Kapor Capital is raising a $125 million fund"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Kapor Capital, the venture firm focused on funding social impact ventures and founders of color, is raising a $125 million fund, called Kapor Capital, Fund III, a source familiar with the situation told TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>What&#8217;s notable about this fund is that it will be the first time Kapor Capital is accepting outside money from investors for a fund. Historically, the capital has come directly from Kapor Capital founders Mitch Kapor and Freada Kapor Klein.<\/p>\n<p>The fund will be led by Kapor Capital partners Brian Dixon and Ulili Onovakpuri. The two will function as co-managing partners.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2117388\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/02\/06\/kapor-capital-promotes-ulili-onovakpuri-to-partner\/\">Onovakpuri was promoted<\/a> from principal to partner back in 2018. At the time, she told me she was interested in technology that makes access to healthcare more accessible, either through reimbursements to low-income people or through subsidized payments. On the people operations side, Onovakpuri said she was looking at investing in startups that help create inclusive cultures.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWhat we have found is that more needs to be done in order to keep [people from diverse backgrounds] in and happy, so that\u2019s what I\u2019ve invested in,\u201d\u00a0Onovakpuri said.<\/p>\n<p>Her first couple of investments were in <a href=\"https:\/\/msurvey.co\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">mSurvey<\/a>, which started as a text message platform to identify disparities in the world, and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.tequitable.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">tEQuitable<\/a>, which aims to help companies be more inclusive.<\/p>\n<p>Her co-manager, Dixon, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2015\/11\/10\/kapor-capital-invests-100000-in-three-people-operations-startups\/\">became one of the first Black investors to be promoted to partner at a venture capital firm in 2015<\/a>. At the time, Dixon told me he was focused on increasing the number of founders who identify as women and\/or an underrepresented person of color in Kapor Capital&#8217;s portfolio to above 50%.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cAs partner, that\u2019s what I\u2019m trying to continue to do,\u201d Dixon said at the time. \u201cWe\u2019re still looking for the best companies. We\u2019re still looking for companies that are going to be impact companies, but also have VC-like returns, so I think that\u2019s what unique about Kapor Capital, is that not many early-stage firms have that focus, and we think we do it pretty well.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Today, 59% of the companies in Kapor Capital&#8217;s portfolio have a founder who identifies as a woman and\/or an underrepresented person of color. Kapor Capital has been instrumental in advancing diversity and inclusion in the tech industry. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2016\/01\/21\/kapor-capital-founders-commitment\/\">Back in 2016<\/a>, for example, Kapor Capital began requiring new portfolio companies to invest in diversity and inclusion as part of a Founders&#8217; Commitment.<\/p>\n<p>Kapor Capital has invested in companies like Blocpower, Bitwise, Promise and Aclima.<\/p>\n<p>Kapor Capital declined to comment for this story.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"DsYoPz9egu\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/30\/freada-kapor-klein-warns-of-vulture-capitalists-during-the-pandemic\/\">Freada Kapor Klein warns of &#8216;vulture capitalists&#8217; during pandemic<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Freada Kapor Klein warns of &#8216;vulture capitalists&#8217; during pandemic&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/30\/freada-kapor-klein-warns-of-vulture-capitalists-during-the-pandemic\/embed\/#?secret=DsYoPz9egu\" data-secret=\"DsYoPz9egu\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Kapor Capital, the venture firm focused on funding social impact ventures and founders of color, is raising a $125 million fund, called Kapor Capital, Fund III, a source familiar with the situation told TechCrunch. the complete agenda for TC Sessions: Justice"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/\">TC Sessions: Justice,<\/a> our second-ever dedicated event to diversity, equity, inclusion and labor in tech, is coming up on March 3, 2021. This is a virtual one-day conference featuring the brightest innovators, leaders and worker-activists in the industry.<\/p>\n<p>We&#8217;re pumped to be able to host Congresswoman Barbara Lee, Backstage Capital founder and Managing Partner Arlan Hamilton, Gig Workers Collective&#8217;s Vanessa Bain, Alphabet Workers Union Executive Chair Parul Koul, Color of Change President Rashad Robinson, Anti-Defamation League CEO Jonathan Greenblatt and others.<\/p>\n<p>In addition to the firesides and panel discussions of the virtual stage, the event will also include networking, startup presentations and the chance to connect with attendees from around the world.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2116312\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Below, you&#8217;ll find the official agenda for <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/\">TC Sessions: Justice.<\/a>\u00a0If you <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#tickets\">want to be a part of this event<\/a>, you can grab a ticket <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#tickets\">here<\/a> for just $5.<\/p>\n<p>If you&#8217;re interested in a sponsored speaking opportunity to join the stage with these fantastic speakers, <a href=\"http:\/\/info.techcrunch.com\/SponsorshipsInterest.html\">contact us here<\/a> to speak with someone from our sales team!<\/p>\n<h1>AGENDA<\/h1>\n<h2>Wednesday, March 3<\/h2>\n<p><strong>State of the Union with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Parul Koul (Google)<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Grace Reckers (Office and Professional Employees International Union)<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Clarissa Redwine (NYU)<\/a><\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Labor unions have been fairly uncommon in tech. That\u2019s finally starting to change in recent years, as workers have pushed to organize at some the industry\u2019s biggest companies, from Alphabet to Kickstarter. Parul Koul\u00a0(Google), Grace Reckers (Office and Professional Employees International Union) and Clarissa Redwine (NYU) will join us to discuss the growing movement.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><strong>Finding the Next Unicorn with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Arlan Hamilton (Backstage Capital)<\/a><\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Arlan Hamilton, the founder and managing partner of Backstage Capital, has raised more than $12 million to back 150 companies led by underrepresented founders. In this session, Hamilton will discuss how she vets the biggest opportunities in investment, and how to disrupt in a positive way.<\/p>\n<p><strong>The Path Forward for Essential Tech Workers with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Vanessa Bain (Gig Workers Collective)<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Jessica E. Martinez (National Council for Occupational Safety and Health)<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Christian Smalls (The Congress of Essential Workers)<\/a><\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Gig workers and warehouse workers have become essential in a pandemic-ravaged economy. In California, a law went into effect earlier this year that makes gig workers independent contractors. Meanwhile, Amazon warehouse workers in Alabama are actively seeking to form a union to ensure better protections at the workplace. You\u2019ll hear from workers and organizers about what\u2019s next for gig workers and tech\u2019s contractor workforce, and what battles lie ahead for these essential workers.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Creating Equity in Tech with Congresswoman Barbara Lee (D-CA)<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>The \u2018pipeline problem\u2019 is often cited as the reason for a lack of diversity in the tech industry. But it\u2019s a myth. Congresswoman Barbara Lee, having represented the East Bay of California for almost a decade, knows all too well about the rise of tech in the Bay Area. We\u2019ll talk with Congresswoman Lee about the opportunities before us to create an equal playing field in tech so that underrepresented investors, founders, designers, coders and the like can reap the benefits.<\/p>\n<p><b>Identifying and Dismantling Tech&#8217;s Deep Systems of Bias with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Haben Girma (Disability Justice Lawyer)<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Mutale Nkonde (AI for the People)<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Safiya Umoja Noble (UCLA)<\/a><\/b><\/p>\n<p>Nearly every popular technology or service has within it systems of bias or exclusion, ignored by the privileged but obvious to the groups affected. How should these systems be exposed and documented, and how can we set about eliminating them and preventing more from appearing in the future? AI for the People&#8217;s Mutale Nkonde, disability rights lawyer Haben Girma and author of &#8220;Algorithms of Oppression&#8221; Safiya Umoja Noble discuss a more inclusive future.<\/p>\n<p>Sponsored by\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Latinx_Startups\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Latinx Startup Alliance<\/a>:<strong> Latinx Founders Leading with Inclusion\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Latinx Founders who are leading with inclusion through diverse teams and\/or supporting a diverse mission, inclusion is a part of their DNA.<\/p>\n<p><b>Founders in Focus with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Tracy Chou (Block Party)<\/a><\/b><\/p>\n<p>We sit down with the founders poised to be the next big disruptors in this industry. Here we chat with Tracy Chou of Block Party, which works to protect people from abuse and harassment online.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Why social media is broken and what to do about it\u00a0with<\/strong> <b><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Naj Austin (Somewhere Good and Ethel&#8217;s Club)<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Jesse Lehrich (Accountable Tech)<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Rashad Robinson (Color of Change)<\/a><\/b><\/p>\n<p>Toxic culture, deadly conspiracies and organized hate have exploded online in recent years. We\u2019ll discuss how much responsibility social networks have in the rise of these phenomena and how to build healthy online communities that make society better, not worse.<\/p>\n<p>Sponsored by\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/startout.org\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">StartOut<\/a>: <strong>The Impact of Out LGBTQ+ Entrepreneurs<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>StartOut and Socos Lab are excited to speak at TechCrunch Justice, and cover the Inclusion Impact Indexes. Its first iteration; the StartOut Pride Economic Impact Index quantifies the economic value of under-utilized LGBTQ+ entrepreneurs. The project looks at entrepreneurs\u2019 economic impact in terms of job creation, patents, financings, and exits in the U.S. Our agenda will be a brief introduction, a demo of the index and its current findings, and a Q&amp;A discussion with the publishers of the index.<\/p>\n<p>Sponsored by\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.onshape.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Onshape<\/a>: <strong>Fireside Chat &#8211; Diversity Is More Than Hiring People of Color<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>It may appear that the country is accepting change \u2013 from racial diversity to equality in the workplace. However, we still have ways to go. For example, organizational diversity is still about hiring from diverse talent pools. In reality, to activate the full potential of diversity, equity, and inclusion (DEI) requires more than a \u201cpeople strategy.\u201d Robust and sustainable work in this area requires embedding DEI principles, policies, systems, and practices into all parts of the business, including the employee and customer experience, brand culture, and overall industry\/corporate citizenship.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Networking Break<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>With our virtual platform, attendees can network via video chat, giving folks the chance to make meaningful connections. CrunchMatch, our algorithmic matching product, will be available to ensure you\u2019re meeting the right people at the show, as well as random matching for attendees who are feeling more adventurous.<\/p>\n<p><b>Demystifying First-Check Fundraising with First-Check Investors with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Brian Brackeen (Lightship Capital)<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Astrid Scholz (Zebras Unite)<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Sydney Thomas (Precursor Ventures)\u00a0<\/a><\/b><\/p>\n<p>There are so many ways to finance your startup that don\u2019t include Y combinator or a traditional fund. In this stacked panel, founders will hear from a trio of decision-makers about how to leverage unconventional communities and resources to get the first dollars they need to execute.<\/p>\n<p><b>Tech in the Era of Accountability with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#1fa16903-b3ec-435b-ba68-d43e00bd8d70\">Jonathan Greenblatt<\/a> (<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#1fa16903-b3ec-435b-ba68-d43e00bd8d70\">Anti-Defamation League<\/a>)\u00a0<\/b><\/p>\n<div>A hands-off approach to moderating online platforms invited hate to flourish in plain sight over the last four years. We\u2019ll speak with Anti-Defamation League CEO Jonathan Greenblatt on proposed policy solutions, if tech is on the cusp of a real era of accountability and what the organization\u2019s mission looks like in 2021 and beyond.<\/div>\n<div><\/div>\n<div><strong style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Meeting of the Minds with Sandra Altine (Facebook),\u00a0 <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Wade Davis (Netflix)<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Bo Young Lee (Uber)<\/a><\/strong><\/div>\n<p>Diversity and inclusion as an idea has been on the agenda of tech companies for years now. But the industry still lacks true inclusion, despite best efforts put forth by heads of diversity, equity and inclusion at these companies. We\u2019ll seek to better understand what\u2019s standing in the way of progress and what it\u2019s going to take to achieve real change.<\/p>\n<p><b>Access All Areas: Designing Accessibility from Day One with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Cynthia Bennett (Carnegie Mellon University)<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Srin Madipalli (formerly of Accomable and Airbnb)<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Mara Mills (NYU)<\/a><\/b><\/p>\n<p>The session will examine the importance of ensuring accessible product design from the beginning. We\u2019ll ask how the social and medical models of disability influence technological evolution. Integrating the expertise of disabled technologists, makers, investors, scientists, software engineers into the DNA of your company from the very beginning is vital to the pursuit of a functioning and equitable society. And could mean you don\u2019t leave money on the table.<\/p>\n<p><b>Reimagining Pathways for Returned Citizens with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Jason Jones (The Last Mile)<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">Deepti Rohatgi (Slack)<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-justice-2021\/#f26d091c-4740-46a5-bac6-55a457c322ef\">and Aly Tamboura (Chan Zuckerberg Initiative)<\/a><\/b><\/p>\n<p>Reentering society after having been incarcerated presents challenges few of us can understand. In this panel, we will examine the role tech can play in ensuring pathways to employment for returned citizens.<\/p>\n<p>\t<iframe\n\t\t\tid=\"wpcom-iframe-97fcb02edc714d7c4ba26638f20b3954\"\n\t\t\twidth=\"99%\"\n\t\t\theight=\"500\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https:\/\/tcprotectedembed.com\/protected-iframe\/97fcb02edc714d7c4ba26638f20b3954\"\n\t\t\tscrolling=\"true\"\n\t\t\tframeborder=\"0\"\n\t\t\tclass=\"wpcom-protected-iframe\"\n\t>\n\t<\/iframe>\n\t<script treatment of AI ethics researchers continues to stir up controversy"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><em>You\u2019ve landed on the web version of the weekly Human Capital newsletter. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\">Sign up here<\/a> to get this in your inbox every Friday at 1 p.m.<\/em><\/p>\n<p>Welcome back to Human Capital. A\u00a0lot happened this week pertaining to on-demand companies like Uber, Postmates, DoorDash and Instacart, and their respective gig workforces. Meanwhile, New York&#8217;s attorney general hit Amazon with a lawsuit over its warehouse labor practices and Twitter made some new commitments to increase diversity at the leadership level by 2025.<\/p>\n<p>But that&#8217;s not all. Google fired another AI top ethicist, Margaret Mitchell. The company also internally published the results of its investigation into what happened with Dr. Timnit Gebru.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2115517\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Apologies in advance for a slightly lengthier than usual newsletter but it&#8217;s all worth knowing, I promise.<\/p>\n<p><em>Quick note: Human Capital is getting a new name because it seems to be causing some confusion, so don&#8217;t be alarmed when this hits your inbox next week with a different name. Name TBD.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<h2><strong>The essential workforce<\/strong><\/h2>\n<h3><b>New bill aims to regulate Amazon warehouses<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">California assemblywoman Lorena Gonzalez, who was behind gig worker bill AB 5, <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.vice.com\/en\/article\/g5bn99\/california-bill-aims-to-regulate-amazons-relentless-warehouse-worker-quotas\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">introduced new legislation<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> that would regulate productivity quotas from companies like Amazon, Walmart and others. Called AB 701, the bill aims to better protect warehouse workers by implementing statewide standards.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cWhile corporations like Amazon are collecting record profits during the pandemic, employees in their warehouses are being expected to do more, go faster and work harder without clear safety standards,\u201d <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/a80.asmdc.org\/press-releases\/assemblywoman-gonzalez-introduces-bill-protect-warehouse-workers-hazardous-working\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Assemblywoman Gonzalez said in a statement<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. \u201cIt\u2019s unacceptable for one the largest and wealthiest employers in the country to put workers\u2019 bodies and lives at risk just so we can get next-day delivery.\u201d<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<h3><b>NY AG sues Amazon<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">New York Attorney General Leticia James <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/ag.ny.gov\/sites\/default\/files\/final_amazon_covid_summons_and_complaint_2-16_as_filed.pdf\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">filed a lawsuit<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> against Amazon for allegedly failing to provide adequate health and safety measures for its workers. As part of the lawsuit, James alleges Amazon retaliated against workers Christian Smalls and Derrick Palmer after they complained to Amazon about the company\u2019s lack of support during the COVID-19 pandemic. James\u2019 suit came after Amazon\u2019s preemptive lawsuit against her office, alleging that workplace safety is not something she has authority over.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/17\/amazon-ny-ag-lawsuit\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">James&#8217; statement<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">: <\/span><\/p>\n<blockquote><p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While Amazon and its CEO made billions during this crisis, hardworking employees were forced to endure unsafe conditions and were retaliated against for rightfully voicing these concerns. Since the pandemic began, it is clear that Amazon has valued profit over people and has failed to ensure the health and safety of its workers. The workers who have powered this country and kept it going during the pandemic are the very workers who continue to be treated the worst. As we seek to hold Amazon accountable for its actions, my office remains dedicated to protecting New York workers from exploitation and unfair treatment in all forms.<\/span><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Meanwhile, of course, Amazon warehouse workers in Bessemer are actively seeking to form a union. <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/grimkim\/status\/1361820493079339008?s=12\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This week<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, reports showed Amazon was altering traffic signals as a way to prevent workers from being able to effectively talk with each other.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><b>Ex-Postmates VP speaks out about the gig economy<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Vikrum Aiyer, the now-former vice president of global public policy and strategic communications at Postmates, <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/16\/ex-postmates-vp-of-global-public-policy-on-the-future-of-gig-work\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">penned a memo<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to his former colleagues and other stakeholders in the gig economy outlining what he thinks needs to happen next in the industry.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In his letter, Aiyer says \u201cit would be a mistake for us to think that mild tweaks to worker classification, or a single state ballot measure, create a durable path forward for meaningfully addressing what Americans truly worry about: the chance to work, take care of their families, and not fret about what comes next.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><b>Postmates drivers say they\u2019ve become prey to scammers<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A new report in The Markup showed scammers sometimes target Postmates workers. In one instance, a scammer stole $346.73 from a worker. You can <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/themarkup.org\/working-for-an-algorithm\/2021\/02\/18\/postmates-drivers-have-become-easy-prey-for-scammers-and-drivers-say-the-companys-not-helping\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">read the full story here<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In related news, Uber, which owns Postmates, <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2021-02-17\/uber-hires-prominent-critic-to-focus-on-treatment-of-drivers?sref=gni836kR\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">recently hired labor researcher and Uber critic<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Alex Rosenblat to lead the company\u2019s marketplace policy, fairness and research efforts.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><b>Uber drivers demand PPE and compensation for time spent sanitizing vehicles<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Bidar411\/status\/1362119559403040768\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Uber drivers shut down Market Street<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> outside of Uber\u2019s San Francisco headquarters to demand the company provide them with enough personal protective equipment during the COVID-19 pandemic. They also want to be compensated for time spent sanitizing vehicles in order to keep themselves and riders safe.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><b>Uber lobbies in the EU for Prop 22-like legislation and loses key battle in the U.K.<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Meanwhile, over in the EU, <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/15\/uber-lobbies-for-prop-22-style-gig-work-standards-in-the-eu\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Uber is lobbying for Prop 22-like standards<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. In a white paper, Uber proposed a \u201cnew standard\u201d for platform work, where it outlines the need to offer some benefits to workers while simultaneously steering away from the possibility of collective bargaining among workers. From TC\u2019s Natasha Lomas:<\/span><\/p>\n<blockquote><p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A universal standard for platform benefits may sound progressive, but the notion of \u201crelevant\u201d benefits for gig workers risks fixing this labor force to a floor far below agreed standards for employment \u2014 closing off any chance of a better deal for a class of workers who are subject to persistent, algorithmic management.<\/span><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>In the U.K., <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/19\/uber-loses-gig-workers-rights-challenge-in-uk-supreme-court\/\">the Supreme Court ruled<\/a> Uber drivers are employees and therefore entitled to minimum wage and holiday pay. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/19\/uber-loses-gig-workers-rights-challenge-in-uk-supreme-court\/\">Also from Lomas<\/a>:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>The case, which\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2016\/10\/28\/uber-loses-employment-tribunal-in-the-uk\/\">dates back to 2016<\/a>, has major ramifications for Uber\u2019s business model (and other gig economy platforms) in the U.K. \u2014 and likely regionally, as similar employment rights challenges are ongoing in European courts.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<h3><b>DoorDash drivers are banding together to decline low-paying orders<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The strategy, <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.vice.com\/en\/article\/3anwdy\/organized-doordash-drivers-declinenow-strategy-is-driving-up-their-pay\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">reported on Vice<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, is designed to beef up the base pay for drivers by working together to game the system.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">From Vice:<\/span><\/p>\n<blockquote><p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The fundamental principles of the official #DECLINENOW movement rely upon all drivers in the movement to exercise their right to use the decline button to decline lowball offers for higher, more feasible ones,\u201d reads a pinned post on the main Facebook group. \u201cDeclining lowball offers forces the algorithm to raise the base pay UP on the declined offer for the next driver as the need for DoorDash to service the order increases. In turn, Dashers will see an increase in higher paying offers, many times doing less deliveries for more money and a much higher paying \u2018Per mile rate.\u2019\u201d<\/span><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<h3><b>Turning jobs into gig work<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/features\/2021-02-17\/gig-economy-coming-for-millions-of-u-s-jobs-after-california-s-uber-lyft-vote?sref=gni836kR\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Bloomberg had a really good feature<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> about how the tech industry\u2019s gig economy is impacting workers in other industries. It\u2019s a must-read, but here&#8217;s a snippet:<\/span><\/p>\n<blockquote><p>Companies in a range of industries could use the Prop 22 model to undermine or eliminate employment protections. A week after the election, Shawn Carolan, a partner at early Uber investor\u00a0<a title=\"Menlo Ventures Management, L.P.\" href=\"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/quote\/17873Z:US\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Menlo Ventures<\/a>, wrote an\u00a0<a title=\"What Proposition 22 Now Makes Possible\" href=\"https:\/\/www.theinformation.com\/articles\/what-proposition-22-now-makes-possible\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">op-ed<\/a> heralding the potential to spread Prop 22\u2019s vision of work \u201cfrom agriculture to zookeeping,\u201d including to \u201cnursing, executive assistance, tutoring, programming, restaurant work and design.\u201d<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<h3><b>President Biden <\/b><a href=\"https:\/\/www.whitehouse.gov\/briefing-room\/statements-releases\/2021\/02\/17\/president-biden-announces-key-nomination-on-jobs-team\/\"><b>nominates Jennifer Abruzzo<\/b><\/a><b> to lead NLRB as general counsel<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Abruzzo is currently the special counsel for strategic initiatives for the Communications Workers of America. For those unfamiliar, CWA has been making a name for itself in the tech industry by helping tech companies like Glitch and Alphabet unionize. Her appointment could prove to be quite beneficial for tech workers and gig workers alike.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In a statement, CWA President Chris Shelton said:<\/span><\/p>\n<blockquote><p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There is no one who has a more thorough grasp of the National Labor Relations Board and the purpose of the National Labor Relations Act than Jennifer Abruzzo. She is a brilliant attorney who understands how the actions of the NLRB impact the daily lives of people at their workplaces. President Biden\u2019s selection of Jennifer as the NLRB General Counsel shows that under his watch, issues affecting working people will be handled by people like Jennifer who have dedicated their lives to helping workers &#8212; and not union busters like we saw during the Trump administration. We hope Jennifer\u2019s confirmation process is speedy &#8212; working people need her at the helm of the NLRB now more than ever.<\/span><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<h3><b>Instacart at odds with workers again<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company has reportedly suspended workers\u2019 accounts for cancelling orders. <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.vice.com\/en\/article\/dy8987\/instacart-temporary-account-suspension-gig-workers-cancel-order\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to Vice<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, these workers said they had good reason to cancel some of these orders, citing things like fears of safety and someone providing the wrong address.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Instacart, however, said it\u2019s part of a fraud prevention policy that places accounts on pause if they suspect fraudulent or suspicious activity.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<h2>Stay woke<\/h2>\n<h3><b>Twitter commits to increasing diversity at leadership level<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/d_lux_brand\/status\/1362514935721250816\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Twitter has committed<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to the Silicon Valley Leadership\u2019s Group 25&#215;25 pledge, which challenges companies to do one of two things:<\/span><\/p>\n<ul>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Either make underrepresented employees 25% of its leadership team by 2025.<\/span><\/li>\n<li>Or increase the number of underrepresented people in leadership positions by 25% by 2025.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Currently, Twitter\u2019s leadership team is just 6.5% Black, 3.9% Latinx, 2.8% multiracial and less than one percent Indigenous, <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/careers.twitter.com\/en\/tweep-life\/diversity.html#item2\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">according to its most recent diversity report<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><b>Examining the \u201cpipeline problem\u201d<\/b><\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As I mentioned last week, I had the pleasure of chatting with Dr. Joy Lisi Rankin, a researcher at AI Now, about her research pertaining to the pipeline problem myth in tech. The story also features some insight from Uber Chief Diversity Officer Bo Young Lee, as well as Paradigm Director Courri Brady.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You can <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/14\/examining-the-pipeline-problem\/\">check that out here<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\"
